<td>\n         <small>\n          51\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (11\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n          <br/>\n          31\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x921\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n         </small>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <small>\n          60\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (16\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n          <br/>\n          38\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (3\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n         </small>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <small>\n          70\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (21\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n          <br/>\n          46\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (8\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n         </small>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <small>\n          78\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (26\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n          <br/>\n          55\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (13\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n         </small>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <small>\n          86\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (30\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n          <br/>\n          64\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (18\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n         </small>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <small>\n          89\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (32\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n          <br/>\n          69\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (21\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n         </small>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <small>\n          87\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (31\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n          <br/>\n          67\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (19\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n         </small>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <small>\n          81\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (27\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n          <br/>\n          60\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (16\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n         </small>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <small>\n          71\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (22\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n          <br/>\n          49\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (9\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n         </small>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <small>\n          61\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (16\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n          <br/>\n          41\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (5\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n         </small>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <small>\n          50\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (10\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n          <br/>\n          32\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n         </small>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="13" style="text-align:center">\n         <i>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_44-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-NOAA-44">\n            [44]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n           <a href="#cite_note-45">\n            [45]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_Cumberland_46-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-NOAA_Cumberland-46">\n            [46]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n           <a href="#cite_note-47">\n            [47]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_Frederick_48-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-NOAA_Frederick-48">\n            [48]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_Baltimore_downtown_49-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-NOAA_Baltimore_downtown-49">\n            [49]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n           <a href="#cite_note-50">\n            [50]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_Ocean_City_51-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-NOAA_Ocean_City-51">\n            [51]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n           <a href="#cite_note-52">\n            [52]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n           <a href="#cite_note-53">\n            [53]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </i>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Adjacent_states">\n        Adjacent states\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Adjacent states">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">\n         Pennsylvania\n        </a>\n        (north)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n         Virginia\n        </a>\n        (south)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia" title="District of Columbia">\n         District of Columbia\n        </a>\n        (south)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">\n         Delaware\n        </a>\n        (east)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">\n         West Virginia\n        </a>\n        (west)\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Maryland" title="History of Maryland">\n        History of Maryland\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="17th_century">\n        17th century\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 17th century">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Calvertcecil.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="297" height="273" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Calvertcecil.jpg/180px-Calvertcecil.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Calvertcecil.jpg/270px-Calvertcecil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cd/Calvertcecil.jpg 2x" width="180"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Calvertcecil.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Cecil_Calvert,_2nd_Baron_Baltimore" title="Cecil Calvert, 2nd Baron Baltimore">\n          Cecil Calvert, 2nd Baron Baltimore\n         </a>\n         , 1st Proprietor of the Maryland colony.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="Maryland\'s_first_colonial_settlement">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Maryland.27s_first_colonial_settlement">\n        Maryland\'s first colonial settlement\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Maryland\'s first colonial settlement">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Maryland" title="Province of Maryland">\n        Province of Maryland\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Catholic\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_Calvert,_1st_Lord_Baltimore" title="George Calvert, 1st Lord Baltimore">\n        George Calvert, 1st Lord Baltimore\n       </a>\n       (1579\xe2\x80\x931632), sought a charter from King\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">\n        Charles I\n       </a>\n       for the territory between\n       <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">\n        Massachusetts\n       </a>\n       to the north and\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       to the immediate south.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stewart_1967_42.E2.80.9343_54-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Stewart_1967_42.E2.80.9343-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After George Calvert died in April 1632, the charter was granted to his son,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cecilius_Calvert,_2nd_Baron_Baltimore" title="Cecilius Calvert, 2nd Baron Baltimore">\n        Cecilius Calvert, 2nd Baron Baltimore\n       </a>\n       (1605\xe2\x80\x931675), on June 20, 1632. Officially, the new "Maryland Colony" was named in honor of\n       <a href="/wiki/Henrietta_Maria_of_France" title="Henrietta Maria of France">\n        Henrietta Maria of France\n       </a>\n       , wife of Charles I of England.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Alternatively, Some Catholic scholars and historians believe Maryland may have been named after Mary, the mother of Jesus, by George Calvert, 1st Lord Baltimore prior to his death in 1632. His original intent may never fully be known. The specific name given in the charter was phrased Terra Mariae, anglice, Maryland. The English name was preferred due to undesired associations of Mariae with the Spanish Jesuit Juan de Mariana, linked to the Inquisition. In addition, Henrietta was never referred to by both her first and middle name. Scholars also agree that under no circumstances was a territory ever named after someone\'s middle name. Many agree\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">\n          <span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (September 2017)">\n           who?\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       that since the original capital of Maryland was\n       <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_City,_Maryland" title="St. Mary\'s City, Maryland">\n        St. Mary\'s City\n       </a>\n       on the north shore of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Potomac_River" title="Potomac River">\n        Potomac River\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 and the county surrounding it, the first erected/created in the province,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       was named\n       <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_County,_Maryland" title="St. Mary\'s County, Maryland">\n        St. Mary\'s County\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 Maryland was most likely named after Mary, the mother of Jesus Christ. The great seal of Maryland also supports this conclusion. The obverse side of the seal reads TERR\xc3\x86 MARI\xc3\x86,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       which translates in Latin as "Land of Mary" instead of TERR\xc3\x86 MARIA, which would acknowledge Henrietta\'s middle name.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Lord Baltimore\'s first settlers arrived in the new colony in March 1634, with his younger brother\n       <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Calvert" title="Leonard Calvert">\n        Leonard Calvert\n       </a>\n       (1606\xe2\x80\x931647), as first provincial\n       <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Maryland" title="Governor of Maryland">\n        Governor of Maryland\n       </a>\n       . They made their first permanent settlement at\n       <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_City,_Maryland" title="St. Mary\'s City, Maryland">\n        St. Mary\'s City\n       </a>\n       in what is now\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_County" title="St. Mary\'s County">\n        St. Mary\'s County\n       </a>\n       . They purchased the site from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Paramount_chief" title="Paramount chief">\n        paramount chief\n       </a>\n       of the region, who was eager to establish trade. St. Mary\'s became the first\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_capital" title="State capital">\n        capital\n       </a>\n       of Maryland, and remained so for 60 years until 1695. More settlers soon followed. Their tobacco crops were successful and quickly made the new colony profitable. However, given the incidence of\n       <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">\n        malaria\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">\n        yellow fever\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Typhoid" title="Typhoid">\n        typhoid\n       </a>\n       , life expectancy in Maryland was about 10 years less than in\n       <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">\n        New England\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iha_59-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-iha-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Persecution_of_Catholics">\n        Persecution of Catholics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Persecution of Catholics">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Plundering_Time" title="Plundering Time">\n        Plundering Time\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Maryland was founded for the purpose of providing religious toleration of England\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">\n        Roman Catholic\n       </a>\n       minority.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washingtonpost.com_60-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost.com-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1642 a number of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puritan" title="Puritan">\n        Puritans\n       </a>\n       left Virginia for Maryland and founded Providence (now called\n       <a href="/wiki/Annapolis,_Maryland" title="Annapolis, Maryland">\n        Annapolis\n       </a>\n       ) on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Shore_of_Maryland" title="Western Shore of Maryland">\n        western shore\n       </a>\n       of the upper\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">\n        Chesapeake Bay\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A dispute with traders from Virginia over\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kent_Island" title="Kent Island">\n        Kent Island\n       </a>\n       in the Chesapeake led to armed conflict. In 1644\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Claiborne" title="William Claiborne">\n        William Claiborne\n       </a>\n       , a Puritan, seized Kent Island while his associate, the pro-Parliament Puritan Richard Ingle, took over St. Mary\'s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Both used religion as a tool to gain popular support. The two years from 1644\xe2\x80\x931646 that Claiborne and his Puritan associates held sway were known as "The Plundering Time". They captured Jesuit priests, imprisoned them, then sent them back to England.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1646 Leonard Calvert returned with troops, recaptured St. Mary\'s City, and restored order. The House of Delegates passed the "Act concerning Religion" in 1649 granting religious liberty to all Trinitarian Christians.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iha_59-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-iha-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1650 the Puritans revolted against the proprietary government. "Protestants swept the Catholics out of the legislature ...and religious strife returned".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iha_59-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-iha-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Puritans set up a new government prohibiting both\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">\n        Roman Catholicism\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">\n        Anglicanism\n       </a>\n       . The Puritan revolutionary government persecuted Maryland Catholics during its reign, known as the "plundering time". Mobs burned down all the original Catholic churches of southern Maryland. The Puritan rule lasted until 1658 when the Calvert family and Lord Baltimore regained proprietary control and re-enacted the Toleration Act.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After England\'s "\n       <a href="/wiki/Glorious_Revolution" title="Glorious Revolution">\n        Glorious Revolution\n       </a>\n       " of 1688, Maryland outlawed Catholicism. This lasted until after the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">\n        American Revolutionary War\n       </a>\n       (1775\xe2\x80\x931783). Wealthy Catholic planters built chapels on their land to practice their religion in relative secrecy.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Border_disputes_(1681\xe2\x80\x931760)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Border_disputes_.281681.E2.80.931760.29">\n        Border disputes (1681\xe2\x80\x931760)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Border disputes (1681\xe2\x80\x931760)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penn%E2%80%93Calvert_Boundary_Dispute" title="Penn\xe2\x80\x93Calvert Boundary Dispute">\n        Penn\xe2\x80\x93Calvert Boundary Dispute\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Cresap%27s_War" title="Cresap\'s War">\n        Cresap\'s War\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The royal charter granted Maryland the land north of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Potomac_River" title="Potomac River">\n        Potomac River\n       </a>\n       up to the\n       <a href="/wiki/40th_parallel_north" title="40th parallel north">\n        40th parallel\n       </a>\n       . A problem arose when\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">\n        Charles II\n       </a>\n       granted a charter for\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">\n        Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       . The grant defined Pennsylvania\'s southern border as identical to Maryland\'s northern border, the 40th parallel. But the grant indicated that Charles II and\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Penn" title="William Penn">\n        William Penn\n       </a>\n       assumed the 40th parallel would pass close to\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Castle,_Delaware" title="New Castle, Delaware">\n        New Castle, Delaware\n       </a>\n       when it falls north of\n       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">\n        Philadelphia\n       </a>\n       , the site of which Penn had already selected for his colony\'s capital city. Negotiations ensued after the problem was discovered in 1681.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A compromise proposed by Charles II in 1682 was undermined by Penn\'s receiving the additional grant of what is now Delaware.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hubbard_63-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-hubbard-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Penn successfully argued that the Maryland charter entitled Lord Baltimore only to unsettled lands, and Dutch settlement in Delaware predated his charter. The dispute remained unresolved for nearly a century, carried on by the descendants of William Penn and Lord Baltimore\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 the\n       <a href="/wiki/Baron_Baltimore" title="Baron Baltimore">\n        Calvert family\n       </a>\n       , which controlled Maryland, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Penn" title="William Penn">\n        Penn family\n       </a>\n       , which controlled Pennsylvania.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hubbard_63-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-hubbard-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The border dispute with Pennsylvania led to Cresap\'s War in the 1730s. Hostilities erupted in 1730 and escalated through the first half of the decade, culminating in the deployment of military forces by Maryland in 1736 and by Pennsylvania in 1737. The armed phase of the conflict ended in May 1738 with the intervention of King George II, who compelled the negotiation of a cease-fire. A provisional agreement had been established in 1732.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hubbard_63-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-hubbard-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Negotiations continued until a final agreement was signed in 1760. The agreement defined the border between Maryland and Pennsylvania as the line of latitude now known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mason%E2%80%93Dixon_line" title="Mason\xe2\x80\x93Dixon line">\n        Mason\xe2\x80\x93Dixon line\n       </a>\n       . Maryland\'s border with Delaware was based on a\n       <a href="/wiki/Transpeninsular_Line" title="Transpeninsular Line">\n        Transpeninsular Line\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Twelve-Mile_Circle" title="Twelve-Mile Circle">\n        Twelve-Mile Circle\n       </a>\n       around New Castle.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hubbard_63-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-hubbard-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="18th_century">\n        18th century\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 18th century">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_in_the_American_Revolution" title="Maryland in the American Revolution">\n        Maryland in the American Revolution\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Most of the English colonists arrived in Maryland as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indentured_servant" title="Indentured servant">\n        indentured servants\n       </a>\n       , and had to serve a several years\' term as laborers to pay for their passage.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the early years, the line between indentured servants and African slaves or laborers was fluid, and white and black laborers commonly lived and worked together, and formed unions.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mixed-race" title="Mixed-race">\n        Mixed-race\n       </a>\n       children born to white mothers were considered free by the principle of\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Partus_sequitur_ventrem" title="Partus sequitur ventrem">\n         partus sequitur ventrem\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , by which children took the social status of their mothers, a principle of slave law that was adopted throughout the colonies, following Virginia in 1662. During the colonial era, families of\n       <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">\n        free people of color\n       </a>\n       were formed most often by unions of white women and African men.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heinegg_65-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Heinegg-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maxime_de_Cromot.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="599" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Maxime_de_Cromot.jpg/220px-Maxime_de_Cromot.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Maxime_de_Cromot.jpg/330px-Maxime_de_Cromot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Maxime_de_Cromot.jpg/440px-Maxime_de_Cromot.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maxime_de_Cromot.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Franco-American_alliance" title="Franco-American alliance">\n          Comte du Bourg\n         </a>\n         (left) and Baron von Closen on their way to Yorktown, September 1781\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Many of the free black families migrated to Delaware, where land was cheaper.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heinegg_65-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Heinegg-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As the flow of indentured laborers to the colony decreased with improving economic conditions in England, planters in Maryland imported thousands more slaves and racial caste lines hardened. The economy\'s growth and prosperity was based on slave labor, devoted first to the production of\n       <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">\n        tobacco\n       </a>\n       as the commodity crop.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Maryland was one of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/13_colonies" title="13 colonies">\n        thirteen colonies\n       </a>\n       that revolted against British rule in the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">\n        American Revolution\n       </a>\n       . On February 2, 1781, Maryland became the 13th state to approve the ratification of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Articles_of_Confederation" title="Articles of Confederation">\n        Articles of Confederation\n       </a>\n       which brought into being the United States as a united,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sovereign" title="Sovereign">\n        sovereign\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Nation_state" title="Nation state">\n        national state\n       </a>\n       . It also became the seventh state admitted to the U.S. after ratifying the new Constitution. In December 1790 Maryland donated land selected by President\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">\n        George Washington\n       </a>\n       to the federal government for the creation of the new national capital of\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">\n        Washington, D.C.\n       </a>\n       The land was provided from\n       <a href="/wiki/Montgomery_County,_Maryland" title="Montgomery County, Maryland">\n        Montgomery\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Prince_George%27s_County,_Maryland" title="Prince George\'s County, Maryland">\n        Prince George\'s\n       </a>\n       counties, as well as from\n       <a href="/wiki/Fairfax_County,_Virginia" title="Fairfax County, Virginia">\n        Fairfax County\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Alexandria,_Virginia" title="Alexandria, Virginia">\n        Alexandria\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       ; however, the land donated by Virginia was later returned to that state by the\n       <a href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia_retrocession" title="District of Columbia retrocession">\n        District of Columbia retrocession\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">\n        19th century\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 19th century">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Original_research" role="presentation">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <div style="width:52px">\n          <img alt="" data-file-height="40" data-file-width="40" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" width="40"/>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n        <td class="mbox-text">\n         <div class="mbox-text-span">\n          This section\n          <b>\n           possibly contains\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research">\n            original research\n           </a>\n          </b>\n          .\n          <span class="hide-when-compact">\n           Please\n           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit">\n            improve it\n           </a>\n           by\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">\n            verifying\n           </a>\n           the claims made and adding\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Inline_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">\n            inline citations\n           </a>\n           . Statements consisting only of original research should be removed.\n          </span>\n          <small>\n           <i>\n            (May 2014)\n           </i>\n          </small>\n          <small class="hide-when-compact">\n           <i>\n            (\n            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">\n             Learn how and when to remove this template message\n            </a>\n            )\n           </i>\n          </small>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ft._Henry_bombardement_1814.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="735" data-file-width="1004" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Ft._Henry_bombardement_1814.jpg/220px-Ft._Henry_bombardement_1814.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Ft._Henry_bombardement_1814.jpg/330px-Ft._Henry_bombardement_1814.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Ft._Henry_bombardement_1814.jpg/440px-Ft._Henry_bombardement_1814.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ft._Henry_bombardement_1814.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The bombardment of\n         <a href="/wiki/Fort_McHenry" title="Fort McHenry">\n          Fort McHenry\n         </a>\n         in Baltimore inspired the song, "\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Star_Spangled_Banner" title="Star Spangled Banner">\n          Star Spangled Banner\n         </a>\n         ".\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Influenced by a changing economy, revolutionary ideals, and preaching by ministers, numerous planters in Maryland freed their slaves in the 20 years after the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">\n        Revolutionary War\n       </a>\n       . Across the Upper South the free black population increased from less than 1% before the war to 14% by 1810.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kolchin_66-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Kolchin-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the\n       <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">\n        War of 1812\n       </a>\n       , the British military attempted to capture Baltimore, which was protected by\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_McHenry" title="Fort McHenry">\n        Fort McHenry\n       </a>\n       . During this bombardment the song "\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Star_Spangled_Banner" title="Star Spangled Banner">\n        Star Spangled Banner\n       </a>\n       " was written by\n       <a href="/wiki/Francis_Scott_Key" title="Francis Scott Key">\n        Francis Scott Key\n       </a>\n       ; it was later adopted as the national anthem.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The National Road (U.S. Hwy 40 today) was authorized in 1817 and ran from Baltimore to St. Louis \xe2\x80\x93 the first federal highway. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_and_Ohio_Railroad" title="Baltimore and Ohio Railroad">\n        Baltimore and Ohio Railroad\n       </a>\n       (B&amp;O) was the first chartered railroad in the United States. It opened its first section of track for regular operation in 1830 between Baltimore and Ellicott City,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dilts_67-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Dilts-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and in 1852 it became the first rail line to reach the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">\n        Ohio River\n       </a>\n       from the eastern seaboard.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stover_68-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Stover-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_War">\n        Civil War\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Civil War">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_in_the_American_Civil_War" title="Maryland in the American Civil War">\n        Maryland in the American Civil War\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The state remained with the Union during the Civil War,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       due in significant part to demographics and Federal intervention. By 1860, 49% of Maryland\'s African Americans were\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_black" title="Free black">\n        free blacks\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kolchin_66-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Kolchin-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Antietam.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="558" data-file-width="800" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Battle_of_Antietam.png/220px-Battle_of_Antietam.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Battle_of_Antietam.png/330px-Battle_of_Antietam.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Battle_of_Antietam.png/440px-Battle_of_Antietam.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Antietam.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Antietam" title="Battle of Antietam">\n          Battle of Antietam\n         </a>\n         was the single bloodiest day of the\n         <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">\n          Civil War\n         </a>\n         with nearly 23,000 casualties.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Holliday_Hicks" title="Thomas Holliday Hicks">\n        Thomas Holliday Hicks\n       </a>\n       suspended the state legislature, and to help ensure the election of a new pro-union governor and legislature, President\n       <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">\n        Abraham Lincoln\n       </a>\n       had a number of its\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fire_eaters" title="Fire eaters">\n        pro-slavery politicians\n       </a>\n       arrested, including the Mayor of Baltimore,\n       <a href="/wiki/George_William_Brown" title="George William Brown">\n        George William Brown\n       </a>\n       ; suspended several civil liberties, including\n       <i>\n        habeas corpus\n       </i>\n       ; and ordered artillery placed on\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Hill,_Baltimore,_Maryland" title="Federal Hill, Baltimore, Maryland">\n        Federal Hill\n       </a>\n       overlooking Baltimore. Historians debate the constitutionality of these wartime actions, and the suspension of civil liberties was later deemed illegal by the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Supreme_Court" title="United States Supreme Court">\n        U.S. Supreme Court\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In April 1861 Federal units and state regiments were attacked as they marched through Baltimore, sparking the\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_riot_of_1861" title="Baltimore riot of 1861">\n        Baltimore riot of 1861\n       </a>\n       , the first bloodshed in the Civil War.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Of the 115,000 men from Maryland who joined the military during the Civil War, 85,000, or 77%, joined the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_army" title="Union army">\n        Union army\n       </a>\n       , while the remainder joined the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Confederate_Army" title="Confederate Army">\n        Confederate Army\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       The largest and most significant battle in the state was the\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Antietam" title="Battle of Antietam">\n        Battle of Antietam\n       </a>\n       on September 17, 1862, near\n       <a href="/wiki/Sharpsburg,_Maryland" title="Sharpsburg, Maryland">\n        Sharpsburg\n       </a>\n       . Although a tactical draw, the battle was considered a strategic Union victory and a\n       <a href="/wiki/Turning_point_of_the_American_Civil_War" title="Turning point of the American Civil War">\n        turning point\n       </a>\n       of the war.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="After_the_war">\n        After the war\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: After the war">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       A new state constitution in 1864\n       <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_States" title="Abolitionism in the United States">\n        abolished\n       </a>\n       slavery, and following passage of constitutional amendments that granted voting rights to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedmen" title="Freedmen">\n        freedmen\n       </a>\n       , in 1867 the state extended suffrage to non-white males.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_Democratic_Party" title="History of the United States Democratic Party">\n        Democratic Party\n       </a>\n       rapidly regained power in the state from\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_Republican_Party" title="History of the United States Republican Party">\n        Republicans\n       </a>\n       . Democrats replaced the Constitution of 1864 with the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maryland_Constitution_of_1867" title="Maryland Constitution of 1867">\n        Constitution of 1867\n       </a>\n       . Following the end of Reconstruction in 1877, Democrats devised means of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disfranchisement_after_Reconstruction_era" title="Disfranchisement after Reconstruction era">\n        disfranchising\n       </a>\n       blacks, initially by physical intimidation and voter fraud, later by constitutional amendments and laws. Blacks and immigrants, however, resisted Democratic Party disfranchisement efforts in the state. Maryland blacks were part of a biracial Republican coalition elected to state government in 1896\xe2\x80\x931904 and comprised 20% of the electorate.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tuck_71-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tuck-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Compared to some other states, blacks were better established both before and after the civil war. Nearly half the population was free before the war, and some had accumulated property. Half the population lived in cities. Literacy was high among blacks and, as Democrats crafted means to exclude them, suffrage campaigns helped reach blacks and teach them how to resist.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tuck_71-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tuck-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Whites did impose\n       <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation" title="Racial segregation">\n        racial segregation\n       </a>\n       in public facilities and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jim_Crow" title="Jim Crow">\n        Jim Crow\n       </a>\n       laws, which effectively lasted until passage of federal civil rights legislation in the mid-1960s.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Baltimore grew significantly during the\n       <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">\n        Industrial Revolution\n       </a>\n       , due in large part to its seaport and good railroad connections, attracting European immigrant labor. Many manufacturing businesses were established in the Baltimore area after the Civil War. Baltimore businessmen, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins" title="Johns Hopkins">\n        Johns Hopkins\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Enoch_Pratt" title="Enoch Pratt">\n        Enoch Pratt\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Peabody" title="George Peabody">\n        George Peabody\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Henry_Walters" title="Henry Walters">\n        Henry Walters\n       </a>\n       , founded notable city institutions that bear their names, including a university, library, music school and art museum.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Cumberland was Maryland\'s second-largest city in the 19th century. Nearby supplies of natural resources along with railroads fostered its growth into a major manufacturing center.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WDL_72-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WDL-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">\n        20th century\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 20th century">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Original_research" role="presentation">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <div style="width:52px">\n          <img alt="" data-file-height="40" data-file-width="40" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" width="40"/>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n        <td class="mbox-text">\n         <div class="mbox-text-span">\n          This section\n          <b>\n           possibly contains\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research">\n            original research\n           </a>\n          </b>\n          .\n          <span class="hide-when-compact">\n           Please\n           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit">\n            improve it\n           </a>\n           by\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">\n            verifying\n           </a>\n           the claims made and adding\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Inline_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">\n            inline citations\n           </a>\n           . Statements consisting only of original research should be removed.\n          </span>\n          <small>\n           <i>\n            (May 2014)\n           </i>\n          </small>\n          <small class="hide-when-compact">\n           <i>\n            (\n            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">\n             Learn how and when to remove this template message\n            </a>\n            )\n           </i>\n          </small>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_20th_century">\n        Early 20th century\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Early 20th century">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Era" title="Progressive Era">\n        Progressive Era\n       </a>\n       of the late 19th and early 20th centuries brought political reforms. In a series of laws passed between 1892 and 1908, reformers worked for standard state-issued ballots (rather than those distributed and marked by the parties); obtained closed voting booths to prevent party workers from "assisting" voters; initiated\n       <a href="/wiki/Primary_election" title="Primary election">\n        primary elections\n       </a>\n       to keep party bosses from selecting candidates; and had candidates listed without party symbols, which discouraged the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illiterate" title="Illiterate">\n        illiterate\n       </a>\n       from participating. These measures worked against ill-educated whites and blacks. Blacks resisted such efforts, with suffrage groups conducting voter education. Blacks defeated three efforts to disfranchise them, making alliances with immigrants to resist various Democratic campaigns.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tuck_71-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tuck-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Disfranchising bills in 1905, 1907, and 1911 were rebuffed, in large part because of black opposition. Blacks comprised 20% of the electorate and immigrants comprised 15%, and the legislature had difficulty devising requirements against blacks that did not also disadvantage immigrants.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tuck_71-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tuck-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Progressive Era also brought reforms in working conditions for Maryland\'s labor force. In 1902 the state regulated conditions in\n       <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">\n        mines\n       </a>\n       ; outlawed\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Child_labor" title="Child labor">\n        child laborers\n       </a>\n       under the age of 12; mandated compulsory school attendance; and enacted the nation\'s first\n       <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_compensation" title="Workers\' compensation">\n        workers\' compensation\n       </a>\n       law. The workers\' compensation law was overturned in the courts, but was redrafted and finally enacted in 1910.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Baltimore_Fire" title="Great Baltimore Fire">\n        Great Baltimore Fire\n       </a>\n       of 1904 burned over 30 hours, destroying 1,526 buildings and spanning 70 city blocks. More than 1,231\n       <a href="/wiki/Firefighter" title="Firefighter">\n        firefighters\n       </a>\n       worked to bring the blaze under control. With the nation\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I#Entry_of_the_United_States" title="World War I">\n        entry into World War I\n       </a>\n       in 1917, new military bases such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_George_G._Meade" title="Fort George G. Meade">\n        Camp Meade\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_Proving_Ground" title="Aberdeen Proving Ground">\n        Aberdeen Proving Ground\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edgewood_Arsenal" title="Edgewood Arsenal">\n        Edgewood Arsenal\n       </a>\n       were established. Existing facilities, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_McHenry" title="Fort McHenry">\n        Fort McHenry\n       </a>\n       , were greatly expanded.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Maryland\'s urban and rural communities had different experiences during the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">\n        Great Depression\n       </a>\n       . The "\n       <a href="/wiki/Bonus_Army" title="Bonus Army">\n        Bonus Army\n       </a>\n       " marched through the state in 1932 on its way to Washington, D.C. Maryland instituted its first ever\n       <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">\n        income tax\n       </a>\n       in 1937 to generate revenue for schools and welfare.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n        <a href="#cite_note-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Baltimore was a major war production center during\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">\n        World War II\n       </a>\n       . The biggest operations were\n       <a href="/wiki/Bethlehem_Steel" title="Bethlehem Steel">\n        Bethlehem Steel\n       </a>\n       \'s Fairfield Yard, which built\n       <a href="/wiki/Liberty_ship" title="Liberty ship">\n        Liberty ships\n       </a>\n       ; and\n       <a href="/wiki/Glenn_L._Martin_Company" title="Glenn L. Martin Company">\n        Glenn Martin\n       </a>\n       , an aircraft manufacturer.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="1950\xe2\x80\x93present">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="1950.E2.80.93present">\n        1950\xe2\x80\x93present\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: 1950\xe2\x80\x93present">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Maryland experienced population growth following World War II, particularly in the Baltimore and Washington, D.C. suburbs. Agricultural tracts gave way to residential communities such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Columbia,_Maryland" title="Columbia, Maryland">\n        Columbia\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Montgomery_Village,_Maryland" title="Montgomery Village, Maryland">\n        Montgomery Village\n       </a>\n       . Concurrently the\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_Highway_System" title="Interstate Highway System">\n        Interstate Highway System\n       </a>\n       was built throughout the state, most notably\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Maryland" title="Interstate 95 in Maryland">\n        I-95\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_495_(Capital_Beltway)" title="Interstate 495 (Capital Beltway)">\n        Capital Beltway\n       </a>\n       , altering travel patterns. In 1952 the eastern and western halves of Maryland were linked for the first time by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge" title="Chesapeake Bay Bridge">\n        Chesapeake Bay Bridge\n       </a>\n       , which replaced a nearby\n       <a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">\n        ferry\n       </a>\n       service.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baybridge.com-history_74-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-baybridge.com-history-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Maryland\'s regions experienced economic changes following WWII. Heavy manufacturing declined in Baltimore. In Maryland\'s four westernmost counties, industrial, railroad, and coal mining jobs declined. On the lower\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Shore_of_Maryland" title="Eastern Shore of Maryland">\n        Eastern Shore\n       </a>\n       , family farms were bought up by major concerns and large-scale poultry farms and vegetable farming became prevalent. In Southern Maryland, tobacco farming nearly vanished due to suburban development and a state tobacco buy-out program.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In an effort to reverse depopulation due to the loss of working-class industries, Baltimore initiated\n       <a href="/wiki/Urban_renewal" title="Urban renewal">\n        urban renewal\n       </a>\n       projects in the 1960s with\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Center" title="Charles Center">\n        Charles Center\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_World_Trade_Center" title="Baltimore World Trade Center">\n        Baltimore World Trade Center\n       </a>\n       . Some resulted in the break-up of intact residential neighborhoods, producing social volatility, and some older residential areas around the harbor have had units renovated and have become popular with new populations.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">\n        Demographics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Demographics">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Maryland" title="List of counties in Maryland">\n        List of counties in Maryland\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_incorporated_places_in_Maryland" title="List of incorporated places in Maryland">\n        List of incorporated places in Maryland\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_census-designated_places_in_Maryland" title="List of census-designated places in Maryland">\n        List of census-designated places in Maryland\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_maryland_counties.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="436" data-file-width="814" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Map_of_maryland_counties.jpg/300px-Map_of_maryland_counties.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Map_of_maryland_counties.jpg/450px-Map_of_maryland_counties.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Map_of_maryland_counties.jpg/600px-Map_of_maryland_counties.jpg 2x" width="300"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_maryland_counties.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Maryland" title="List of counties in Maryland">\n          Maryland\'s counties\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_Maryland_USA.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="617" data-file-width="1128" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Regions_of_Maryland_USA.gif/300px-Regions_of_Maryland_USA.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Regions_of_Maryland_USA.gif/450px-Regions_of_Maryland_USA.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Regions_of_Maryland_USA.gif/600px-Regions_of_Maryland_USA.gif 2x" width="300"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_Maryland_USA.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Geographic regions of Maryland\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">\n        United States Census Bureau\n       </a>\n       estimates that the population of Maryland was 6,006,401 on July 1, 2015, a 4.03% increase since the\n       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">\n        2010 United States Census\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_75-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2015 Maryland had an estimated population of 6,006,401, which is an increase of 29,994, from the prior year and an increase of 232,849, or 4.03% percent, since 2010. This includes a natural increase since the last census of 189,158 people (that is 464,251 births minus 275,093 deaths) and an increase due to net migration of 116,713 people into the state.\n       <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Immigration to the United States">\n        Immigration\n       </a>\n       from outside the United States resulted in a net increase of 129,730 people, and migration within the country produced a net loss of 13,017 people.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Center_of_population" title="Center of population">\n        center of population\n       </a>\n       of Maryland is located on the county line between\n       <a href="/wiki/Anne_Arundel_County,_Maryland" title="Anne Arundel County, Maryland">\n        Anne Arundel County\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Howard_County,_Maryland" title="Howard County, Maryland">\n        Howard County\n       </a>\n       , in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_area" title="Unincorporated area">\n        unincorporated community\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Jessup,_Maryland" title="Jessup, Maryland">\n        Jessup\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Maryland\'s history as a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Border_states_(Civil_War)" title="Border states (Civil War)">\n        border state\n       </a>\n       has led it to exhibit characteristics of both the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northern_United_States" title="Northern United States">\n        Northern\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">\n        Southern\n       </a>\n       regions of the United States. Generally, rural\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Maryland" title="Western Maryland">\n        Western Maryland\n       </a>\n       between the\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Panhandle_of_West_Virginia" title="Eastern Panhandle of West Virginia">\n        West Virginian Panhandle\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">\n        Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       has an\n       <a href="/wiki/Appalachia" title="Appalachia">\n        Appalachian\n       </a>\n       culture; the\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Maryland" title="Southern Maryland">\n        Southern\n       </a>\n       and Eastern Shore regions of Maryland embody a\n       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_Southern_United_States" title="Culture of the Southern United States">\n        Southern culture\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n        <a href="#cite_note-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       while densely populated Central Maryland\xe2\x80\x94radiating outward from\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">\n        Baltimore\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">\n        Washington, D.C.\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94has more in common with that of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">\n        Northeast\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">\n        <a href="#cite_note-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The U.S. Census Bureau designates Maryland as one of the\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_States" title="South Atlantic States">\n        South Atlantic States\n       </a>\n       , but it is commonly associated with the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_States" title="Mid-Atlantic States">\n        Mid-Atlantic States\n       </a>\n       and/or\n       <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">\n        Northeastern United States\n       </a>\n       by other federal agencies, the media, and some residents.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_79-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPA_80-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EPA-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FBI_81-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FBI-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amtrak_82-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-amtrak-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-princeton_83-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-princeton-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_data">\n        Birth data\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Birth data">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       As of 2011, 58.0 percent of Maryland\'s population younger than age 1 were non-white.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">\n        <a href="#cite_note-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Note: Births in table don\'t add up, because Hispanics are counted both by their ethnicity and by their race, giving a higher overall number.\n       </i>\n      </p>\n <b>\n          73,616\n         </b>\n         (100%)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Language">\n        Language\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Language">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language_in_the_United_States" title="Spanish language in the United States">\n        Spanish\n       </a>\n       (including\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish-based_creole_languages" title="Spanish-based creole languages">\n        Spanish Creole\n       </a>\n       ) is the second-most-spoken language in Maryland, after\n       <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">\n        English\n       </a>\n       . The third- and fourth-most-spoken languages are\n       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">\n        French\n       </a>\n       (including\n       <a href="/wiki/Patois" title="Patois">\n        Patois\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Cajun_French" title="Cajun French">\n        Cajun\n       </a>\n       ) and\n       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">\n        Chinese\n       </a>\n       . Other commonly spoken languages include various\n       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Africa" title="Languages of Africa">\n        African languages\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">\n        Korean\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">\n        German\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">\n        Tagalog\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">\n        Russian\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_language" title="Vietnamese language">\n        Vietnamese\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">\n        Italian\n       </a>\n       , various\n       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Asia" title="Languages of Asia">\n        Asian languages\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">\n        Persian\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">\n        Hindi\n       </a>\n       and other\n       <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">\n        Indic languages\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">\n        Greek\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">\n        Arabic\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">\n        <a href="#cite_note-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Settlements">\n        Settlements\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Settlements">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_statistical_areas" title="Maryland statistical areas">\n        Maryland statistical areas\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maryland_population_map.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="700" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Maryland_population_map.png/350px-Maryland_population_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Maryland_population_map.png/525px-Maryland_population_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f5/Maryland_population_map.png 2x" width="350"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maryland_population_map.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Maryland\'s population is concentrated mostly in the Baltimore and Washington metropolitan areas.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Most of the population of Maryland lives in the central region of the state, in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_Metropolitan_Area" title="Baltimore Metropolitan Area">\n        Baltimore Metropolitan Area\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_Metropolitan_Area" title="Washington Metropolitan Area">\n        Washington Metropolitan Area\n       </a>\n       , both of which are part of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore-Washington_Metropolitan_Area" title="Baltimore-Washington Metropolitan Area">\n        Baltimore-Washington Metropolitan Area\n       </a>\n       . The majority of Maryland\'s population is concentrated in the cities and suburbs surrounding\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">\n        Washington, D.C.\n       </a>\n       , as well as in and around Maryland\'s most populous city,\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">\n        Baltimore\n       </a>\n       . Historically, these and many other Maryland cities developed along the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fall_Line" title="Fall Line">\n        Fall Line\n       </a>\n       , the line along which rivers, brooks, and streams are interrupted by rapids and/or waterfalls. Maryland\'s capital city,\n       <a href="/wiki/Annapolis,_Maryland" title="Annapolis, Maryland">\n        Annapolis\n       </a>\n       , is one exception to this pattern, since it lies along the banks of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Severn_River_(Maryland)" title="Severn River (Maryland)">\n        Severn River\n       </a>\n       , close to where it empties into the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">\n        Chesapeake Bay\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Eastern Shore is less populous and more rural, as are the counties of western Maryland. The two\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Maryland" title="Western Maryland">\n        westernmost\n       </a>\n       counties of Maryland,\n       <a href="/wiki/Allegany_County,_Maryland" title="Allegany County, Maryland">\n        Allegany\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Garrett_County,_Maryland" title="Garrett County, Maryland">\n        Garrett\n       </a>\n       , are mountainous and sparsely populated, resembling West Virginia and\n       <a href="/wiki/Appalachia" title="Appalachia">\n        Appalachia\n       </a>\n       more than they do the rest of Maryland. Both eastern and western Maryland are, however, dotted with cities of regional importance, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Ocean_City,_Maryland" title="Ocean City, Maryland">\n        Ocean City\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Princess_Anne,_Maryland" title="Princess Anne, Maryland">\n        Princess Anne\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Salisbury,_Maryland" title="Salisbury, Maryland">\n        Salisbury\n       </a>\n       on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Shore_of_Maryland" title="Eastern Shore of Maryland">\n        Eastern Shore\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Cumberland,_Maryland" title="Cumberland, Maryland">\n        Cumberland\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Frostburg,_Maryland" title="Frostburg, Maryland">\n        Frostburg\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hancock,_Maryland" title="Hancock, Maryland">\n        Hancock\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Maryland" title="Western Maryland">\n        Western Maryland\n       </a>\n       . Southern Maryland is still somewhat rural, but suburbanization from Washington, D.C. has encroached significantly since the 1960s; important local population centers include\n       <a href="/wiki/Lexington_Park,_Maryland" title="Lexington Park, Maryland">\n        Lexington Park\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Prince_Frederick,_Maryland" title="Prince Frederick, Maryland">\n        Prince Frederick\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Waldorf,_Maryland" title="Waldorf, Maryland">\n        Waldorf\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">\n        <a href="#cite_note-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">\n        <a href="#cite_note-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <br/>\n      </p>\n      <table class="navbox">\n       <tr>\n        <th class="navbox-title" colspan="10">\n         <div
