Mormon\n          </td>\n          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">\n           <div style="background:red; width:1%; overflow: hidden;">\n           </div>\n          </td>\n          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">\n           1%\n          </td>\n         </tr>\n         <tr>\n          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">\n           Orthodox Christian\n          </td>\n          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">\n           <div style="background:cyan; width:1%; overflow: hidden;">\n           </div>\n          </td>\n          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">\n           1%\n          </td>\n         </tr>\n        </table>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BasilicaExterior.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1112" data-file-width="1200" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/BasilicaExterior.jpg/220px-BasilicaExterior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/BasilicaExterior.jpg/330px-BasilicaExterior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/BasilicaExterior.jpg/440px-BasilicaExterior.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BasilicaExterior.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_Basilica" title="Baltimore Basilica">\n          Baltimore Basilica\n         </a>\n         was the first\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">\n          Catholic\n         </a>\n         <a href="/wiki/Cathedral" title="Cathedral">\n          cathedral\n         </a>\n         built in the\n         <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n          U.S.\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       According to Pew research 69 percent of Maryland\'s population identifies as Christian.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pew_Religion_and_Politics_116-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Pew_Religion_and_Politics-116">\n         [116]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The largest religious groups in Maryland as of 2010 were: the\n       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">\n        Catholic Church\n       </a>\n       with 837,338 adherents in Maryland, followed by non-denominational\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evangelical_Protestant" title="Evangelical Protestant">\n        Evangelical Protestants\n       </a>\n       with 298,921 members, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist_Church" title="United Methodist Church">\n        United Methodist Church\n       </a>\n       with 238,774. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention" title="Southern Baptist Convention">\n        Southern Baptist Convention\n       </a>\n       has 150,345 members.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.thearda.com_117-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-www.thearda.com-117">\n         [117]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">\n        Judaism\n       </a>\n       is the largest non-Christian religion in Maryland with 241,000 adherents, or 4 percent of the total population.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">\n        <a href="#cite_note-118">\n         [118]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">\n        Seventh-day Adventist Church\n       </a>\n       \'s World Headquarters and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">\n        Ahmadiyya\n       </a>\n       Muslims national Headquarters is located in\n       <a href="/wiki/Silver_Spring,_Maryland" title="Silver Spring, Maryland">\n        Silver Spring\n       </a>\n       , just outside the District of Columbia.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Maryland has been prominent in U.S. Catholic tradition, partially because it was intended by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_Calvert" title="George Calvert">\n        George Calvert\n       </a>\n       as a haven for English Catholics. Baltimore was the seat of the first Catholic bishop in the U.S. (1789), and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emmitsburg" title="Emmitsburg">\n        Emmitsburg\n       </a>\n       was the home and burial place of the first American-born citizen to be\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canonized" title="Canonized">\n        canonized\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Elizabeth_Ann_Seton" title="St. Elizabeth Ann Seton">\n        St. Elizabeth Ann Seton\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_University" title="Georgetown University">\n        Georgetown University\n       </a>\n       , the first Catholic University, was founded in 1789 in what was then part of Maryland.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">\n        <a href="#cite_note-119">\n         [119]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basilica_of_the_National_Shrine_of_the_Assumption_of_the_Virgin_Mary" title="Basilica of the National Shrine of the Assumption of the Virgin Mary">\n        Basilica of the National Shrine of the Assumption of the Virgin Mary\n       </a>\n       in Baltimore was the first Roman Catholic cathedral built in the United States, and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Baltimore" title="Archbishop of Baltimore">\n        Archbishop of Baltimore\n       </a>\n       is, albeit without formal primacy, the United States\' quasi-\n       <a href="/wiki/Primate_(bishop)" title="Primate (bishop)">\n        primate\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       and often a cardinal. Among the immigrants of the 19th and 20th century from eastern and southern Europe were many Catholics.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">\n        Economy\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Economy">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Business_in_Maryland" title="Business in Maryland">\n        Business in Maryland\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_federal_installations_in_Maryland" title="List of federal installations in Maryland">\n        List of federal installations in Maryland\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_shopping_malls_in_Maryland" title="List of shopping malls in Maryland">\n        List of shopping malls in Maryland\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maryland_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="Maryland locations by per capita income">\n        Maryland locations by per capita income\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Baltoport.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="637" data-file-width="1365" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Baltoport.jpg/280px-Baltoport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Baltoport.jpg/420px-Baltoport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Baltoport.jpg/560px-Baltoport.jpg 2x" width="280"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Baltoport.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The Port of Baltimore\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Economic_Analysis" title="Bureau of Economic Analysis">\n        Bureau of Economic Analysis\n       </a>\n       estimates that Maryland\'s gross state product in 2012 was $317.7 billion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gross_State_Product_MD_120-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Gross_State_Product_MD-120">\n         [120]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, Maryland has been using\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genuine_Progress_Indicator" title="Genuine Progress Indicator">\n        Genuine Progress Indicator\n       </a>\n       , an indicator of well-being, to guide the state\'s development, rather than relying only on growth indicators like GDP.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">\n        <a href="#cite_note-121">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">\n        <a href="#cite_note-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       According to the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">\n        U.S. Census Bureau\n       </a>\n       , Maryland households are currently the wealthiest in the country, with a 2013 median household income of $72,483\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">\n        <a href="#cite_note-123">\n         [123]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       which puts it ahead of\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">\n        New Jersey\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">\n        Connecticut\n       </a>\n       , which are second and third respectively. Two of Maryland\'s counties, Howard and Montgomery, are the second and eleventh\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Highest-income_counties_in_the_United_States" title="Highest-income counties in the United States">\n        wealthiest counties in the nation\n       </a>\n       respectively. Maryland ranked No. 1 with the most millionaires per capita in 2013, with a ratio of 7.7 percent.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">\n        <a href="#cite_note-124">\n         [124]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Also, the state\'s poverty rate of 7.8 percent is the lowest in the country.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">\n        <a href="#cite_note-125">\n         [125]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">\n        <a href="#cite_note-126">\n         [126]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">\n        <a href="#cite_note-127">\n         [127]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_personal_income_in_the_United_States" title="Per capita personal income in the United States">\n        per capita personal income\n       </a>\n       in 2006 was $43,500, fifth in the nation. As of May 2014, the state\'s unemployment rate was 5.5 percent.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">\n        <a href="#cite_note-128">\n         [128]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Geo_Map_of_Median_Income_by_Location_in_Maryland.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="882" data-file-width="1208" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Geo_Map_of_Median_Income_by_Location_in_Maryland.png/220px-Geo_Map_of_Median_Income_by_Location_in_Maryland.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Geo_Map_of_Median_Income_by_Location_in_Maryland.png/330px-Geo_Map_of_Median_Income_by_Location_in_Maryland.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Geo_Map_of_Median_Income_by_Location_in_Maryland.png/440px-Geo_Map_of_Median_Income_by_Location_in_Maryland.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Geo_Map_of_Median_Income_by_Location_in_Maryland.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A map showing Maryland\'s median income by county. Data is sourced from the\n         <a class="external text" href="http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/acs/" rel="nofollow">\n          2014 ACS 5-year Estimate\n         </a>\n         report published by the\n         <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">\n          US Census Bureau\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Maryland\'s economy benefits from the state\'s close proximity to the federal government in\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">\n        Washington, D.C.\n       </a>\n       with an emphasis on technical and administrative tasks for the defense/aerospace industry and bio-research laboratories, as well as staffing of satellite government headquarters in the suburban or exurban Baltimore/Washington area. Ft. Meade serves as the headquarters of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Defense_Information_Systems_Agency" title="Defense Information Systems Agency">\n        Defense Information Systems Agency\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Cyber_Command" title="United States Cyber Command">\n        United States Cyber Command\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Agency" title="National Security Agency">\n        National Security Agency\n       </a>\n       /\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_Security_Service" title="Central Security Service">\n        Central Security Service\n       </a>\n       . In addition, a number of educational and medical research institutions are located in the state. In fact, the various components of The\n       <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Johns Hopkins University">\n        Johns Hopkins University\n       </a>\n       and its medical research facilities are now the largest single employer in the Baltimore area. Altogether,\n       <a href="/wiki/White-collar_worker" title="White-collar worker">\n        white collar\n       </a>\n       technical and administrative workers comprise 25 percent of Maryland\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labor_force" title="Labor force">\n        labor force\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       attributable in part to nearby Maryland being a part of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_Metro_Area" title="Washington Metro Area">\n        Washington Metro Area\n       </a>\n       where the federal government office employment is relatively high.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Manufacturing, while large in dollar value, is highly diversified with no sub-sector contributing over 20 percent of the total. Typical forms of manufacturing include electronics, computer equipment, and chemicals. The once mighty primary metals sub-sector, which at one time included what was then the largest steel factory in the world at\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sparrows_Point" title="Sparrows Point">\n        Sparrows Point\n       </a>\n       , still exists, but is pressed with foreign competition,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bankruptcy" title="Bankruptcy">\n        bankruptcies\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merger" title="Merger">\n        mergers\n       </a>\n       . During World War II the Glenn Martin Company (now part of\n       <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">\n        Lockheed Martin\n       </a>\n       ) airplane factory employed some 40,000 people.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Mining other than construction materials is virtually limited to coal, which is located in the mountainous western part of the state. The brownstone quarries in the east, which gave Baltimore and Washington much of their characteristic architecture in the mid-19th century, were once a predominant natural resource. Historically, there used to be small gold-mining operations in Maryland, some near Washington, but these no longer exist.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Baltimore_port">\n        Baltimore port\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Baltimore port">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       One major service activity is transportation, centered on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Baltimore" title="Port of Baltimore">\n        Port of Baltimore\n       </a>\n       and its related\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Railroad" title="Railroad">\n        rail\n       </a>\n       and trucking access. The port ranked 17th in the U.S. by tonnage in 2008.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">\n        <a href="#cite_note-129">\n         [129]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Although the port handles a wide variety of products, the most typical imports are raw materials and bulk commodities, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Iron_ore" title="Iron ore">\n        iron ore\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">\n        petroleum\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">\n        sugar\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">\n        fertilizers\n       </a>\n       , often distributed to the relatively close manufacturing centers of the inland\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Midwest" title="Midwest">\n        Midwest\n       </a>\n       via good overland transportation. The port also receives several different brands of imported motor vehicles and is the number one auto port in the U.S.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">\n        <a href="#cite_note-130">\n         [130]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Baltimore City is the eighth largest port in the nation, and was at the center of the February 2006\n       <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Ports_World_controversy" title="Dubai Ports World controversy">\n        controversy\n       </a>\n       over the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dubai_Ports_World" title="Dubai Ports World">\n        Dubai Ports World\n       </a>\n       deal because it was considered to be of such strategic importance. The state as a whole is heavily industrialized, with a booming economy and influential technology centers. Its computer industries are some of the most sophisticated in the United States, and the federal government has invested heavily in the area. Maryland is home to several large military bases and scores of high level government jobs.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chesapeake_and_Delaware_Canal" title="Chesapeake and Delaware Canal">\n        Chesapeake and Delaware Canal\n       </a>\n       is a 14 miles (23\xc2\xa0km)\n       <a href="/wiki/Canal" title="Canal">\n        canal\n       </a>\n       on the Eastern Shore that connects the waters of the Delaware River with those of the Chesapeake Bay, and in particular with the Port of Baltimore, carrying 40 percent of the port\'s ship traffic.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">\n        <a href="#cite_note-131">\n         [131]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture_and_fishing">\n        Agriculture and fishing\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Agriculture and fishing">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Maryland has a large food-production sector. A large component of this is commercial\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_freshwater_fishes_of_Maryland" title="List of freshwater fishes of Maryland">\n        fishing\n       </a>\n       , centered in the Chesapeake Bay, but also including activity off the short Atlantic seacoast. The largest catches by species are the\n       <a href="/wiki/Callinectes_sapidus" title="Callinectes sapidus">\n        blue crab\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oysters" title="Oysters">\n        oysters\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Striped_bass" title="Striped bass">\n        striped bass\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Menhaden" title="Menhaden">\n        menhaden\n       </a>\n       . The Bay also has overwintering waterfowl in its wildlife refuges. The waterfowl support a\n       <a href="/wiki/Birdwatching" title="Birdwatching">\n        tourism sector of sportsmen\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CarrollCountyMD.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="220" data-file-width="325" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/CarrollCountyMD.jpg/220px-CarrollCountyMD.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/CarrollCountyMD.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CarrollCountyMD.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Agriculture is an important part of the state\'s economy\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Maryland has large areas of fertile agricultural land in its coastal and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Piedmont_Plateau" title="Piedmont Plateau">\n        Piedmont\n       </a>\n       zones, though this land use is being encroached upon by urbanization. Agriculture is oriented to dairy farming (especially in foothill and piedmont areas) for nearby large city milksheads plus specialty perishable horticulture crops, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Cucumber" title="Cucumber">\n        cucumbers\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Watermelon" title="Watermelon">\n        watermelons\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Sweet_corn" title="Sweet corn">\n        sweet corn\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">\n        tomatoes\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Muskmelon" title="Muskmelon">\n        muskmelons\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Squash_(fruit)" title="Squash (fruit)">\n        squash\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peas" title="Peas">\n        peas\n       </a>\n       (Source:USDA Crop Profiles). In addition, the southern counties of the western shoreline of Chesapeake Bay are warm enough to support a\n       <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">\n        tobacco\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Cash_crop" title="Cash crop">\n        cash crop\n       </a>\n       zone, which has existed since early Colonial times but declined greatly after a state government buyout in the 1990s. There is also a large automated\n       <a href="/wiki/Chicken" title="Chicken">\n        chicken\n       </a>\n       -farming sector in the state\'s southeastern part;\n       <a href="/wiki/Salisbury,_Maryland" title="Salisbury, Maryland">\n        Salisbury\n       </a>\n       is home to\n       <a href="/wiki/Perdue_Farms" title="Perdue Farms">\n        Perdue Farms\n       </a>\n       . Maryland\'s food-processing plants are the most significant type of manufacturing by value in the state.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Biotechnology">\n        Biotechnology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Biotechnology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Maryland is a major center for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_sciences" title="Life sciences">\n        life sciences\n       </a>\n       research and development. With more than 400 biotechnology companies located there, Maryland is the fourth-largest nexus in this field in the United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">\n        <a href="#cite_note-132">\n         [132]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Institutions and government agencies with an interest in research and development located in Maryland include the\n       <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Johns Hopkins University">\n        Johns Hopkins University\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Applied_Physics_Laboratory" title="Johns Hopkins Applied Physics Laboratory">\n        Johns Hopkins Applied Physics Laboratory\n       </a>\n       , more than one campus of the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_System_of_Maryland" title="University System of Maryland">\n        University System of Maryland\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Goddard_Space_Flight_Center" title="Goddard Space Flight Center">\n        Goddard Space Flight Center\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">\n        United States Census Bureau\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health">\n        National Institutes of Health\n       </a>\n       (NIH), the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Standards_and_Technology" title="National Institute of Standards and Technology">\n        National Institute of Standards and Technology\n       </a>\n       (NIST), the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Mental_Health" title="National Institute of Mental Health">\n        National Institute of Mental Health\n       </a>\n       (NIMH), the\n       <a href="/wiki/Walter_Reed_National_Military_Medical_Center" title="Walter Reed National Military Medical Center">\n        Walter Reed National Military Medical Center\n       </a>\n       , the federal\n       <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration" title="Food and Drug Administration">\n        Food and Drug Administration\n       </a>\n       (FDA), the\n       <a href="/wiki/Howard_Hughes_Medical_Institute" title="Howard Hughes Medical Institute">\n        Howard Hughes Medical Institute\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celera_Genomics" title="Celera Genomics">\n        Celera Genomics\n       </a>\n       company, the\n       <a href="/wiki/J._Craig_Venter_Institute" title="J. Craig Venter Institute">\n        J. Craig Venter Institute\n       </a>\n       (JCVI), and\n       <a href="/wiki/MedImmune" title="MedImmune">\n        MedImmune\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 recently purchased by\n       <a href="/wiki/AstraZeneca" title="AstraZeneca">\n        AstraZeneca\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Defense_contractors">\n        Defense contractors\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Defense contractors">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Maryland is home to defense contractor\n       <a href="/wiki/Emergent_BioSolutions" title="Emergent BioSolutions">\n        Emergent BioSolutions\n       </a>\n       , which manufactures and provides an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anthrax_vaccine" title="Anthrax vaccine">\n        anthrax vaccine\n       </a>\n       to U.S. government military personnel. As of April 2014, Emergent had sold over 66 million doses of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BioThrax" title="BioThrax">\n        BioThrax\n       </a>\n       to the U.S. government.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">\n        <a href="#cite_note-133">\n         [133]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <i>\n        Forbes\n       </i>\n       recognized Emergent as the top performing company in the state of Maryland for the 2015\xe2\x80\x932016 fiscal year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">\n        <a href="#cite_note-134">\n         [134]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">\n        Tourism\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Tourism">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ocean_City_MD_beach_looking_north_from_pier.jpeg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Ocean_City_MD_beach_looking_north_from_pier.jpeg/220px-Ocean_City_MD_beach_looking_north_from_pier.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Ocean_City_MD_beach_looking_north_from_pier.jpeg/330px-Ocean_City_MD_beach_looking_north_from_pier.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Ocean_City_MD_beach_looking_north_from_pier.jpeg/440px-Ocean_City_MD_beach_looking_north_from_pier.jpeg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ocean_City_MD_beach_looking_north_from_pier.jpeg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The beach resort town of Ocean City along the Atlantic Ocean is a popular tourist destination in Maryland\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Tourism is popular in Maryland, with tourists visiting the city attractions of Baltimore, the beach attractions of the Eastern Shore, and the nature attractions of western Maryland, as well as many passing through en route to Washington, D.C. Baltimore attractions include the\n       <a href="/wiki/Harborplace" title="Harborplace">\n        Harborplace\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_Aquarium" title="Baltimore Aquarium">\n        Baltimore Aquarium\n       </a>\n       , as well as the popular\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Camden_Yards" title="Camden Yards">\n        Camden Yards\n       </a>\n       baseball stadium.\n       <a href="/wiki/Ocean_City,_Maryland" title="Ocean City, Maryland">\n        Ocean City\n       </a>\n       on the Atlantic Coast has been a popular beach destination in summer, particularly since the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge" title="Chesapeake Bay Bridge">\n        Chesapeake Bay Bridge\n       </a>\n       was built in 1952 connecting the Eastern Shore to the more populated Maryland cities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baybridge.com-history_74-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-baybridge.com-history-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">\n        Transportation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Transportation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Department_of_Transportation" title="Maryland Department of Transportation">\n        Maryland Department of Transportation\n       </a>\n       , headquartered in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hanover,_Maryland" title="Hanover, Maryland">\n        Hanover\n       </a>\n       area of\n       <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_area" title="Unincorporated area">\n        unincorporated\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Anne_Arundel_County,_Maryland" title="Anne Arundel County, Maryland">\n        Anne Arundel County\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">\n        <a href="#cite_note-135">\n         [135]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       oversees most transportation in the state through its various administration-level agencies. The independent\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Transportation_Authority" title="Maryland Transportation Authority">\n        Maryland Transportation Authority\n       </a>\n       , headquartered in Baltimore, maintains and operates the state\'s eight toll facilities.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">\n        Roads\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Roads">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Interstate_Highways_in_Maryland" title="List of Interstate Highways in Maryland">\n        List of Interstate Highways in Maryland\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Maryland_state_highways" title="List of Maryland state highways">\n        List of Maryland state highways\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_minor_Maryland_state_highways" title="List of minor Maryland state highways">\n        List of minor Maryland state highways\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_former_Maryland_state_highways" title="List of former Maryland state highways">\n        List of former Maryland state highways\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Maryland\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_Highway_System" title="Interstate Highway System">\n        Interstate highways\n       </a>\n       include 110 miles (180\xc2\xa0km) of\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Maryland" title="Interstate 95 in Maryland">\n        Interstate\xc2\xa095\n       </a>\n       (I-95), which enters the northeast portion of the state, travels through\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">\n        Baltimore\n       </a>\n       , and becomes part of the eastern section of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_495_(Capital_Beltway)" title="Interstate 495 (Capital Beltway)">\n        Capital Beltway\n       </a>\n       to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson_Bridge" title="Woodrow Wilson Bridge">\n        Woodrow Wilson Bridge\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_68_in_Maryland" title="Interstate 68 in Maryland">\n        I-68\n       </a>\n       travels 81 miles (130\xc2\xa0km), connecting the western portions of the state to\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_70_in_Maryland" title="Interstate 70 in Maryland">\n        I-70\n       </a>\n       at the small town of Hancock. I-70 enters from Pennsylvania north of Hancock and continues east for 93 miles (150\xc2\xa0km) to Baltimore, connecting\n       <a href="/wiki/Hagerstown,_Maryland" title="Hagerstown, Maryland">\n        Hagerstown\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Frederick,_Maryland" title="Frederick, Maryland">\n        Frederick\n       </a>\n       along the way.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_83_in_Maryland" title="Interstate 83 in Maryland">\n        I-83\n       </a>\n       has 34 miles (55\xc2\xa0km) in Maryland and connects Baltimore to southern central Pennsylvania (\n       <a href="/wiki/Harrisburg,_Pennsylvania" title="Harrisburg, Pennsylvania">\n        Harrisburg\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/York,_Pennsylvania" title="York, Pennsylvania">\n        York, Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       ). Maryland also has an 11-mile (18\xc2\xa0km) portion of\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_81_in_Maryland" title="Interstate 81 in Maryland">\n        I-81\n       </a>\n       that travels through the state near Hagerstown.\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_97" title="Interstate 97">\n        I-97\n       </a>\n       , fully contained within Anne Arundel County and the second shortest (17.6 miles (28.3\xc2\xa0km)) one- or two-digit Interstate highway which connects the Baltimore area to the Annapolis area. Hawaii has one that is shorter.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">\n          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (May 2014)">\n           clarification needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There are also several\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_auxiliary_Interstate_Highways" title="List of auxiliary Interstate Highways">\n        auxiliary Interstate highways\n       </a>\n       in Maryland. Among them are two beltways encircling the major cities of the region:\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_695_(Maryland)" title="Interstate 695 (Maryland)">\n        I-695\n       </a>\n       , the McKeldin (Baltimore) Beltway, which encircles Baltimore; and a portion of\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_495_(Capital_Beltway)" title="Interstate 495 (Capital Beltway)">\n        I-495\n       </a>\n       , the Capital Beltway, which encircles Washington, D.C.\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_270_(Maryland)" title="Interstate 270 (Maryland)">\n        I-270\n       </a>\n       , which connects the Frederick area with Northern Virginia and the District of Columbia through major suburbs to the northwest of Washington, is a major commuter route and is as wide as fourteen lanes at points.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Both I-270 and the Capital Beltway were extremely\n       <a href="/wiki/Traffic_congestion" title="Traffic congestion">\n        congested\n       </a>\n       ; however, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intercounty_Connector" title="Intercounty Connector">\n        Intercounty Connector\n       </a>\n       (ICC;\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_200" title="Maryland Route 200">\n        MD\xc2\xa0200\n       </a>\n       ) alleviated some of the congestion over time. Construction of the ICC was a major part of the campaign platform of former Governor\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Ehrlich" title="Robert Ehrlich">\n        Robert Ehrlich\n       </a>\n       , who was in office from 2003 until 2007, and of Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Martin_O%27Malley" title="Martin O\'Malley">\n        Martin O\'Malley\n       </a>\n       , who succeeded him.\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_595_(Maryland)" title="Interstate 595 (Maryland)">\n        I-595\n       </a>\n       , which is an\n       <a href="/wiki/Unsigned_highway" title="Unsigned highway">\n        unsigned highway\n       </a>\n       concurrent with\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_50_in_Maryland" title="U.S. Route 50 in Maryland">\n        US\xc2\xa050\n       </a>\n       /\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_301_in_Maryland" title="U.S. Route 301 in Maryland">\n        US\xc2\xa0301\n       </a>\n       , is the longest unsigned interstate in the country and connects\n       <a href="/wiki/Prince_George%27s_County,_Maryland" title="Prince George\'s County, Maryland">\n        Prince George\'s County\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_D.C." title="Washington D.C.">\n        Washington D.C.\n       </a>\n       with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annapolis" title="Annapolis">\n        Annapolis\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Shore_of_Maryland" title="Eastern Shore of Maryland">\n        Eastern Shore\n       </a>\n       via the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge" title="Chesapeake Bay Bridge">\n        Chesapeake Bay Bridge\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2700" data-file-width="1793" height="256" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge.jpg/170px-Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge.jpg/255px-Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge.jpg/340px-Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge" title="Chesapeake Bay Bridge">\n          Chesapeake Bay Bridge\n         </a>\n         connects Maryland\'s\n         <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Shore_of_Maryland" title="Eastern Shore of Maryland">\n          Eastern\n         </a>\n         and\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Shore" title="Western Shore">\n          Western\n         </a>\n         Shores.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Maryland also has a\n       <a href="/wiki/State_highway" title="State highway">\n        state highway\n       </a>\n       system that contains routes numbered from 2 through 999, however most of the higher-numbered routes are either unsigned or are relatively short. Major state highways include Routes\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_2" title="Maryland Route 2">\n        2\n       </a>\n       (Governor Ritchie Highway/Solomons Island Road/Southern Maryland Blvd.),\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_4" title="Maryland Route 4">\n        4\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Avenue_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="Pennsylvania Avenue (Washington, D.C.)">\n        Pennsylvania Avenue\n       </a>\n       /Southern Maryland Blvd./Patuxent Beach Road/St. Andrew\'s Church Road),\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_5" title="Maryland Route 5">\n        5\n       </a>\n       (Branch Avenue/Leonardtown Road/Point Lookout Road),\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_32" title="Maryland Route 32">\n        32\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_45" title="Maryland Route 45">\n        45\n       </a>\n       (York Road),\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_97" title="Maryland Route 97">\n        97\n       </a>\n       (Georgia Avenue),\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_100" title="Maryland Route 100">\n        100\n       </a>\n       (Paul T. Pitcher Memorial Highway),\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_210" title="Maryland Route 210">\n        210\n       </a>\n       (Indian Head Highway),\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_235" title="Maryland Route 235">\n        235\n       </a>\n       (Three Notch Road),\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_295" title="Maryland Route 295">\n        295\n       </a>\n       (Baltimore-Washington Parkway),\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_355" title="Maryland Route 355">\n        355\n       </a>\n       (Wisconsin Avenue/Rockville Pike/Frederick Road),\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_404" title="Maryland Route 404">\n        404\n       </a>\n       (Queen Anne Highway/ Shore Highway), and\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_650" title="Maryland Route 650">\n        650\n       </a>\n       (New Hampshire Avenue).\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">\n        Airports\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Airports">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Aviation_in_Maryland" title="Aviation in Maryland">\n        Aviation in Maryland\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Maryland" title="List of airports in Maryland">\n        List of airports in Maryland\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Maryland\'s largest airport is\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore-Washington_International_Thurgood_Marshall_Airport" title="Baltimore-Washington International Thurgood Marshall Airport">\n        Baltimore-Washington International Thurgood Marshall Airport\n       </a>\n       , more commonly referred to as BWI. The airport is named for the Baltimore-born\n       <a href="/wiki/Thurgood_Marshall" title="Thurgood Marshall">\n        Thurgood Marshall\n       </a>\n       , the first African-American\n       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">\n        Supreme Court justice\n       </a>\n       . The only other airports with commercial service are at\n       <a href="/wiki/Hagerstown_Regional_Airport" title="Hagerstown Regional Airport">\n        Hagerstown\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wicomico_Regional_Airport" title="Wicomico Regional Airport">\n        Salisbury\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Maryland suburbs of Washington, D.C. are also served by the other two airports in the region,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan_Washington_National_Airport" title="Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport">\n        Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dulles_International_Airport" title="Dulles International Airport">\n        Dulles International Airport\n       </a>\n       , both in\n       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Virginia" title="Northern Virginia">\n        Northern Virginia\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/College_Park_Airport" title="College Park Airport">\n        College Park Airport\n       </a>\n       is the nation\'s oldest, founded in 1909, and is still used.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wilbur_Wright" title="Wilbur Wright">\n        Wilbur Wright\n       </a>\n       trained military aviators at this location.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">\n        <a href="#cite_note-136">\n         [136]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">\n        <a href="#cite_note-137">\n         [137]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">\n        Rail\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Rail">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Maryland_railroads" title="List of Maryland railroads">\n        List of Maryland railroads\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">\n        Amtrak\n       </a>\n       trains, including the high speed\n       <a href="/wiki/Acela_Express" title="Acela Express">\n        Acela Express\n       </a>\n       serve Baltimore\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Station_(Baltimore)" title="Pennsylvania Station (Baltimore)">\n        Penn Station\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BWI_Rail_Station" title="BWI Rail Station">\n        BWI Airport\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Carrollton_(Washington_Metro)" title="New Carrollton (Washington Metro)">\n        New Carrollton\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aberdeen_(Amtrak_station)" title="Aberdeen (Amtrak station)">\n        Aberdeen\n       </a>\n       along the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_D.C." title="Washington D.C.">\n        Washington D.C.\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">\n        Boston\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Corridor" title="Northeast Corridor">\n        Northeast Corridor\n       </a>\n       . In addition, train service is provided to\n       <a href="/wiki/Rockville,_Maryland" title="Rockville, Maryland">\n        Rockville\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Cumberland,_Maryland" title="Cumberland, Maryland">\n        Cumberland\n       </a>\n       by Amtrak\'s Washington, D.C., to\n       <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">\n        Chicago\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capitol_Limited_(Amtrak)" title="Capitol Limited (Amtrak)">\n        Capitol Limited\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ellicott_City_Station_1970.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3225" data-file-width="4098" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Ellicott_City_Station_1970.jpg/220px-Ellicott_City_Station_1970.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Ellicott_City_Station_1970.jpg/330px-Ellicott_City_Station_1970.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Ellicott_City_Station_1970.jpg/440px-Ellicott_City_Station_1970.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ellicott_City_Station_1970.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Ellicott_City_Station" title="Ellicott City Station">\n          Ellicott City Station\n         </a>\n         , on the original B&amp;O Railroad line, is the oldest remaining passenger station in the United States. The rail line is still used by\n         <a href="/wiki/CSX_Transportation" title="CSX Transportation">\n          CSX Transportation\n         </a>\n         for freight trains, and the station is now a museum.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WMATA" title="WMATA">\n        WMATA\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington_Metro" title="Washington Metro">\n        Metrorail\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">\n        rapid transit\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Metrobus_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="Metrobus (Washington, D.C.)">\n        Metrobus\n       </a>\n       local bus systems (the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_rapid_transit_systems_by_ridership" title="List of United States rapid transit systems by ridership">\n        2nd\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_local_bus_agencies_by_ridership" title="List of United States local bus agencies by ridership">\n        6th\n       </a>\n       busiest in the nation of their respective modes) provide service in Montgomery and Prince George\'s counties and connect them to Washington D.C., with the express Metrobus\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Route_B30_(WMATA)" title="Route B30 (WMATA)">\n        <i>\n         Route B30\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       serving\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BWI_Thurgood_Marshall_Airport" title="BWI Thurgood Marshall Airport">\n        BWI Airport\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Transit_Administration" title="Maryland Transit Administration">\n        Maryland Transit Administration\n       </a>\n       (often abbreviated as "MTA Maryland"), a state agency part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Department_of_Transportation" title="Maryland Department of Transportation">\n        Maryland Department of Transportation\n       </a>\n       also provides transit services within the state. Headquartered in Baltimore, MTA\'s transit services are largely focused on central Maryland, as well as some portions of the Eastern Shore and Southern MD. Baltimore\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_Light_Rail" title="Baltimore Light Rail">\n        Light Rail\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Metro_Subway" title="Baltimore Metro Subway">\n        Metro Subway\n       </a>\n       systems serve its densely populated inner-city and the surrounding suburbs. The MTA also serves the city and its suburbs with its\n       <a href="/wiki/MTA_Maryland_bus_service" title="MTA Maryland bus service">\n        local bus\n       </a>\n       service (the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_local_bus_agencies_by_ridership" title="List of United States local bus agencies by ridership">\n        9th largest system\n       </a>\n       in the nation). The MTA\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Transit_Administration#Commuter_bus" title="Maryland Transit Administration">\n        Commuter Bus\n       </a>\n       system provides express coach service on longer routes connecting Washington D.C. and Baltimore to parts of Central and Southern MD as well as the Eastern Shore. The commuter rail service, known as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maryland_Area_Rail_Commuter" title="Maryland Area Rail Commuter">\n        MARC\n       </a>\n       , operates three lines which all terminate at\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington_Union_Station" title="Washington Union Station">\n        Washington Union Station\n       </a>\n       and provide service to Baltimore\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_Penn_Station" title="Baltimore Penn Station">\n        Penn\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Camden_Station" title="Camden Station">\n        Camden\n       </a>\n       stations,\n       <a href="/wiki/Perryville,_Maryland" title="Perryville, Maryland">\n        Perryville\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Frederick,_Maryland" title="Frederick, Maryland">\n        Frederick\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Martinsburg,_West_Virginia" title="Martinsburg, West Virginia">\n        Martinsburg, WV\n       </a>\n       . In addition, many suburban counties operate their own local bus systems which connect to and complement the larger MTA and WMATA/Metro services.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freight_rail_transport" title="Freight rail transport">\n        Freight rail transport\n       </a>\n       is handled principally by two\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Class_I_railroad" title="Class I railroad">\n        Class I railroads\n       </a>\n       , as well as several smaller regional and local carriers.\n       <a href="/wiki/CSX_Transportation" title="CSX Transportation">\n        CSX Transportation\n       </a>\n       has more extensive\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rail_tracks" title="Rail tracks">\n        trackage\n       </a>\n       throughout the state, with 560 miles (900\xc2\xa0km),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSXT_138-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CSXT-138">\n         [138]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       followed by\n       <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Southern_Railway" title="Norfolk Southern Railway">\n        Norfolk Southern Railway\n       </a>\n       . Major\n       <a href="/wiki/Rail_yard" title="Rail yard">\n        rail yards\n       </a>\n       are located in Baltimore and Cumberland,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSXT_138-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CSXT-138">\n         [138]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       with an\n       <a href="/wiki/Intermodal_freight_transport" title="Intermodal freight transport">\n        intermodal\n       </a>\n       terminal (rail, truck and marine) in Baltimore.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">\n        <a href="#cite_note-139">\n         [139]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_government">\n        Law and government\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Law and government">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maryland_quarter,_reverse_side,_2000.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1105" data-file-width="1106" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Maryland_quarter%2C_reverse_side%2C_2000.jpg/170px-Maryland_quarter%2C_reverse_side%2C_2000.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Maryland_quarter%2C_reverse_side%2C_2000.jpg/255px-Maryland_quarter%2C_reverse_side%2C_2000.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Maryland_quarter%2C_reverse_side%2C_2000.jpg/340px-Maryland_quarter%2C_reverse_side%2C_2000.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maryland_quarter,_reverse_side,_2000.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The reverse side of the Maryland quarter shows the dome of the State House in Annapolis.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Maryland" title="Government of Maryland">\n        Government of Maryland\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Maryland" title="List of Governors of Maryland">\n        List of Governors of Maryland\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Army_National_Guard" title="Maryland Army National Guard">\n        Maryland Army National Guard\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Air_National_Guard" title="Maryland Air National Guard">\n        Maryland Air National Guard\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Maryland" title="Government of Maryland">\n        government of Maryland\n       </a>\n       is conducted according to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maryland_Constitution" title="Maryland Constitution">\n        state constitution\n       </a>\n       . The government of Maryland, like the other 49\n       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_United_States#State_government" title="Politics of the United States">\n        state governments\n       </a>\n       , has exclusive authority over matters that lie entirely within the state\'s borders, except as limited by the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_United_States" title="Constitution of the United States">\n        Constitution of the United States\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Power in Maryland is divided among three branches of government:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_branch" title="Executive branch">\n        executive\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_branch" title="Legislative branch">\n        legislative\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judicial_branch" title="Judicial branch">\n        judicial\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_General_Assembly" title="Maryland General Assembly">\n        Maryland General Assembly\n       </a>\n       is composed of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_House_of_Delegates" title="Maryland House of Delegates">\n        Maryland House of Delegates\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Senate" title="Maryland Senate">\n        Maryland Senate\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Maryland" title="Governor of Maryland">\n        Maryland\'s governor\n       </a>\n       is unique in the United States as the office is vested with significant authority in budgeting. The legislature may not increase the governor\'s proposed budget expenditures. Unlike many other states, significant autonomy is granted to many of Maryland\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">\n        counties\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Most of the business of government is conducted in\n       <a href="/wiki/Annapolis,_Maryland" title="Annapolis, Maryland">\n        Annapolis\n       </a>\n       , the state\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capital_(political)" title="Capital (political)">\n        capital\n       </a>\n       . Elections for governor and most statewide offices, as well as most county elections, are held in\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_midterm_election" title="United States midterm election">\n        midterm-election years\n       </a>\n       (even-numbered years not divisible by four).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The judicial branch of state government consists of one united District Court of Maryland that sits in every county and Baltimore City, as well as 24 Circuit Courts sitting in each County and Baltimore City, the latter being courts of general jurisdiction for all civil disputes over $30,000.00, all equitable jurisdiction and major criminal proceedings. The intermediate appellate court is known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Court_of_Special_Appeals" title="Maryland Court of Special Appeals">\n        Court of Special Appeals\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/State_supreme_court" title="State supreme court">\n        state supreme court\n       </a>\n       is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Court_of_Appeals" title="Maryland Court of Appeals">\n        Court of Appeals\n       </a>\n       . The appearance of the judges of the Maryland Court of Appeals is unique; Maryland is the only state whose judges wear red robes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">\n        <a href="#cite_note-140">\n         [140]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Taxation">\n        Taxation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Taxation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Maryland imposes five\n       <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">\n        income tax\n       </a>\n       brackets, ranging from 2 to 6.25 percent of personal income.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">\n        <a href="#cite_note-141">\n         [141]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The city of Baltimore and Maryland\'s 23 counties levy local "piggyback" income taxes at rates between 1.25 and 3.2 percent of Maryland taxable income. Local officials set the rates and the revenue is returned to the local governments quarterly. The top income tax bracket of 9.45 percent is the fifth highest combined state and local income tax rates in the country, behind New York City\'s 11.35 percent, California\'s 10.3 percent, Rhode Island\'s 9.9 percent, and Vermont\'s 9.5 percent.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">\n        <a href="#cite_note-142">\n         [142]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Maryland\'s state\n       <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">\n        sales tax\n       </a>\n       is 6 percent.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       All real property in Maryland is subject to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Property_tax" title="Property tax">\n        property tax\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       Generally, properties that are owned and used by religious, charitable, or educational organizations or property owned by the federal, state or local governments are exempt.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       Property tax rates vary widely.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       No restrictions or limitations on property taxes are imposed by the state, meaning cities and counties can set tax rates at the level they deem necessary to fund governmental services.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       If a proposed tax rate increases the total property tax revenues, the governing body must advertise that fact and hold a public hearing on the new tax rate, which is called the Constant Yield Tax Rate process.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">\n        Elections\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Elections">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Maryland" title="Politics of Maryland">\n        Politics of Maryland\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_Maryland" title="Political party strength in Maryland">\n        Political party strength in Maryland\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spiro_Agnew.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1878" data-file-width="1464" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Spiro_Agnew.jpg/170px-Spiro_Agnew.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Spiro_Agnew.jpg/255px-Spiro_Agnew.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Spiro_Agnew.jpg/340px-Spiro_Agnew.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spiro_Agnew.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Spiro_Agnew" title="Spiro Agnew">\n          Spiro Agnew\n         </a>\n         , former\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Vice_President" title="United States Vice President">\n          United States Vice President\n         </a>\n         , is the highest-ranking political leader from Maryland since the founding of the United States\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="float:right; margin:1em; font-size:95%;">\n       <caption>\n        Gubernatorial election results\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leip.2C_David_143-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Leip.2C_David-143">\n          [143]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </caption>\n       <tr Republican\n         </a>\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td align="center" style="background:#FFB6B6">\n         <a class="new"
