Maryland\'s elections have been largely controlled by the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Democratic_Party" title="U.S. Democratic Party">\n        Democrats\n       </a>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       State elections are dominated\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">\n          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (April 2017)">\n           when?\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       by Baltimore and the populous suburban counties bordering\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">\n        Washington, D.C.\n       </a>\n       :\n       <a href="/wiki/Montgomery_County,_Maryland" title="Montgomery County, Maryland">\n        Montgomery\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Prince_George%27s_County,_Maryland" title="Prince George\'s County, Maryland">\n        Prince George\'s\n       </a>\n       . Forty-three percent of the state\'s population resides\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">\n          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (April 2017)">\n           when?\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       in these three jurisdictions, each of which contain large, traditionally Democratic\n       <a href="/wiki/Voting_bloc" title="Voting bloc">\n        voting bloc(s)\n       </a>\n       :\n       <a href="/wiki/African_Americans" title="African Americans">\n        African Americans\n       </a>\n       in Baltimore and Prince George\'s,\n       <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">\n        federal\n       </a>\n       employees in Prince George\'s and Montgomery, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Postgraduate_education" title="Postgraduate education">\n        postgraduates\n       </a>\n       in Montgomery. The remainder of the state, particularly\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Maryland" title="Western Maryland">\n        Western Maryland\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Shore_of_Maryland" title="Eastern Shore of Maryland">\n        Eastern Shore\n       </a>\n       , is more supportive of\n       <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">\n        Republicans\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       Maryland\xc2\xb4s best known political figure\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">\n          <span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (April 2017)">\n           according to whom?\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       is a Republican \xe2\x80\x93 former Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Spiro_Agnew" title="Spiro Agnew">\n        Spiro Agnew\n       </a>\n       , who served as United States Vice President under\n       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">\n        Richard Nixon\n       </a>\n       as Vice President from 1969 to 1973, when he resigned in the aftermath of revelations that he had taken\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bribes" title="Bribes">\n        bribes\n       </a>\n       while he was Governor of Maryland. In late 1973 a court found Agnew guilty of violating tax laws.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1980, Maryland was one of six states to vote for\n       <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">\n        Jimmy Carter\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       In recent\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words">\n          <span title="Who says this? (April 2017)">\n           weasel\xc2\xa0words\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       years, Maryland has been among the most reliable states for Democratic nominees.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       In 1992,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">\n        Bill Clinton\n       </a>\n       fared better in Maryland than any other state except his home state of\n       <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">\n        Arkansas\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       In 1996, Maryland was Clinton\'s sixth best, in 2000 Maryland ranked fourth for Gore and in 2004\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">\n        John Kerry\n       </a>\n       showed his fifth-best performance in Maryland.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       In 2008\n       <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">\n        Barack Obama\n       </a>\n       won the state\'s 10 electoral votes with 61.9 percent of the vote to\n       <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">\n        John McCain\n       </a>\n       \'s 36.5 percent.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       As of September 2016\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , Maryland supported the Democratic nominee in each of the last six presidential elections, by an average margin of 15.4 percent.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Both of Maryland\'s U.S. Senators and seven of its eight Representatives in Congress are\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">\n          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (April 2017)">\n           when?\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       Democrats, and Democrats hold a\n       <a href="/wiki/Supermajority" title="Supermajority">\n        supermajority\n       </a>\n       in the state Senate.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2002, former Governor\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Ehrlich" title="Robert Ehrlich">\n        Robert Ehrlich\n       </a>\n       was the first Republican to be elected to that office in four decades, and after one term lost his seat to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_Mayor" title="Baltimore Mayor">\n        Baltimore Mayor\n       </a>\n       and Democrat\n       <a href="/wiki/Martin_O%27Malley" title="Martin O\'Malley">\n        Martin O\'Malley\n       </a>\n       . Ehrlich ran again for governor in 2010, losing again to O\'Malley.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The 2006 election brought no change in the pattern of Democratic dominance. After Democratic Senator\n       <a href="/wiki/Paul_Sarbanes" title="Paul Sarbanes">\n        Paul Sarbanes\n       </a>\n       announced that he was retiring, Democratic Congressman\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benjamin_Cardin" title="Benjamin Cardin">\n        Benjamin Cardin\n       </a>\n       defeated Republican Lieutenant Governor\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michael_S._Steele" title="Michael S. Steele">\n        Michael S. Steele\n       </a>\n       , with 55 percent of the vote, against Steele\'s 44 percent.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       While Republicans usually win more counties, by piling up large margins in the west and east, they are also usually swamped by the more densely populated and heavily Democratic Baltimore-Washington axis. In 2008, for instance, McCain won 17 counties to Obama\'s six; Obama also carried Baltimore City. While McCain won most of the western and eastern counties by margins of 2-to-1 or more, he was almost completely shut out in the larger counties surrounding Baltimore and Washington; every large county except Anne Arundel went for Obama.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">\n        <a href="#cite_note-144">\n         [144]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       From 2007 to 2011 U.S. Congressman\n       <a href="/wiki/Steny_Hoyer" title="Steny Hoyer">\n        Steny Hoyer\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland%27s_5th_congressional_district" title="Maryland\'s 5th congressional district">\n        MD-5\n       </a>\n       ), a\n       <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">\n        Democrat\n       </a>\n       , was elected as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Majority_Leader" title="Majority Leader">\n        Majority Leader\n       </a>\n       for the\n       <a href="/wiki/110th_United_States_Congress" title="110th United States Congress">\n        110th Congress\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">\n        House of Representatives\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/111th_United_States_Congress" title="111th United States Congress">\n        111th Congress\n       </a>\n       , serving in that post. His district covers parts of\n       <a href="/wiki/Anne_Arundel_County,_Maryland" title="Anne Arundel County, Maryland">\n        Anne Arundel\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Prince_George%27s_County,_Maryland" title="Prince George\'s County, Maryland">\n        Prince George\'s\n       </a>\n       counties, in addition to all of\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_County,_Maryland" title="Charles County, Maryland">\n        Charles\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Calvert_County,_Maryland" title="Calvert County, Maryland">\n        Calvert\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Mary%27s_County,_Maryland" title="Saint Mary\'s County, Maryland">\n        St. Mary\'s\n       </a>\n       counties in\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Maryland" title="Southern Maryland">\n        southern Maryland\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">\n        <a href="#cite_note-145">\n         [145]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2010 Republicans won control of most counties. The Democratic Party remained in control of eight county governments including\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_City" title="Baltimore City">\n        Baltimore City\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">\n        <a href="#cite_note-146">\n         [146]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2014\n       <a href="/wiki/Larry_Hogan" title="Larry Hogan">\n        Larry Hogan\n       </a>\n       , a Republican, was elected Governor of Maryland.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">\n        <a href="#cite_note-147">\n         [147]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Hogan is the second Republican to become the Governor of Maryland since Spiro Agnew\'s resigned in 1969 to become Vice President.\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align: center;float:right;">\n       <tr>\n        <th colspan="6">\n         Voter Registration by Party (May 2017)\n         <sup 3,928,689\n        </th>\n        <th style="text-align:center;">\n         100%\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">\n        Media\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Media">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg">\n          <img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14"  <div class="mbox-text-span">\n          <b>\n           This section needs expansion\n          </b>\n          .\n          <small>\n           You can help by\n           <a class="external text"        (March 2017)\n           </i>\n          </small>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Maryland has many popular sources of media. A well known newspaper is\n       <i>\n        The Baltimore Sun\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Category:Maryland_media" title="Category:Maryland media">\n        Category:Maryland media\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">\n        Education\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Education">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_and_secondary_education">\n        Primary and secondary education\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Primary and secondary education">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_school_districts_in_Maryland" title="List of school districts in Maryland">\n        List of school districts in Maryland\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_high_schools_in_Maryland" title="List of high schools in Maryland">\n        List of high schools in Maryland\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Arts_and_culture_of_Maryland" title="Arts and culture of Maryland">\n        Arts and culture of Maryland\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Memorial_Chapel_at_UMCP,_front_view_off-center,_August_21,_2006.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3237" data-file-width="2410" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Memorial_Chapel_at_UMCP%2C_front_view_off-center%2C_August_21%2C_2006.jpg/170px-Memorial_Chapel_at_UMCP%2C_front_view_off-center%2C_August_21%2C_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Memorial_Chapel_at_UMCP%2C_front_view_off-center%2C_August_21%2C_2006.jpg/255px-Memorial_Chapel_at_UMCP%2C_front_view_off-center%2C_August_21%2C_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Memorial_Chapel_at_UMCP%2C_front_view_off-center%2C_August_21%2C_2006.jpg/340px-Memorial_Chapel_at_UMCP%2C_front_view_off-center%2C_August_21%2C_2006.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Memorial_Chapel_at_UMCP,_front_view_off-center,_August_21,_2006.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Memorial Chapel at the\n         <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland,_College_Park" title="University of Maryland, College Park">\n          University of Maryland, College Park\n         </a>\n         , Maryland\'s largest university.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Education Week ranked Maryland #1 in its nationwide 2009\xe2\x80\x932013 Quality Counts reports.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2014)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       The College Board\'s 9th Annual AP Report to the Nation also ranked Maryland first.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2014)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       Primary and secondary education in Maryland is overseen by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_State_Department_of_Education" title="Maryland State Department of Education">\n        Maryland State Department of Education\n       </a>\n       , which is headquartered in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore,_Maryland" title="Baltimore, Maryland">\n        Baltimore\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">\n        <a href="#cite_note-149">\n         [149]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The highest educational official in the state is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Superintendent_(education)" title="Superintendent (education)">\n        State Superintendent of Schools\n       </a>\n       , who is appointed by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Board_of_education" title="Board of education">\n        State Board of Education\n       </a>\n       to a four-year term of office. The Maryland General Assembly has given the Superintendent and State Board autonomy to make educationally related decisions, limiting its own influence on the day-to-day functions of public education. Each county and county-equivalent in Maryland has a\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_school_districts_in_Maryland" title="List of school districts in Maryland">\n        local Board of Education\n       </a>\n       charged with running the public schools in that particular jurisdiction.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The budget for education was $5.5 billion in 2009, representing about 40 percent of the state\'s general fund.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">\n        <a href="#cite_note-150">\n         [150]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Maryland has a broad range of private primary and secondary schools. Many of these are affiliated with various religious sects, including\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parochial_schools" title="Parochial schools">\n        parochial schools\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">\n        Catholic Church\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quaker" title="Quaker">\n        Quaker\n       </a>\n       schools,\n       <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">\n        Seventh-day Adventist\n       </a>\n       schools, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">\n        Jewish\n       </a>\n       schools. In 2003, Maryland law was changed to allow for the creation of publicly funded charter schools, although the charter schools must be approved by their local Board of Education and are not exempt from state laws on education, including collective bargaining laws.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2008 the state led the entire country in the percentage of students passing\n       <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Placement" title="Advanced Placement">\n        Advanced Placement\n       </a>\n       examinations. 23.4 percent of students earned passing grades on the AP tests given in May 2008. This marks the first year that Maryland earned this honor.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">\n        <a href="#cite_note-151">\n         [151]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Three Maryland high schools (in Montgomery County) were ranked among the top 100 in the country by US News in 2009, based in large part on AP test scores.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">\n        <a href="#cite_note-152">\n         [152]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">\n        Colleges and universities\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Maryland" title="List of colleges and universities in Maryland">\n        List of colleges and universities in Maryland\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Maryland has several historic and renowned private colleges and universities, the most prominent of which is\n       <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Johns Hopkins University">\n        Johns Hopkins University\n       </a>\n       , founded in 1876 with a grant from Baltimore entrepreneur\n       <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins" title="Johns Hopkins">\n        Johns Hopkins\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The first public university in the state is the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland,_Baltimore" title="University of Maryland, Baltimore">\n        University of Maryland, Baltimore\n       </a>\n       , which was founded in 1807 and contains the University of Maryland\'s only public academic\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland_School_of_Medicine" title="University of Maryland School of Medicine">\n        health\n       </a>\n       , human services, and one of two\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland_School_of_Law" title="University of Maryland School of Law">\n        law centers\n       </a>\n       (the other being the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Baltimore_School_of_Law" title="University of Baltimore School of Law">\n        University of Baltimore School of Law\n       </a>\n       ). Seven professional and graduate schools train the majority of the state\'s physicians, nurses, dentists, lawyers, social workers, and pharmacists.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">\n        <a href="#cite_note-153">\n         [153]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The largest undergraduate institution in Maryland is the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland,_College_Park" title="University of Maryland, College Park">\n        University of Maryland, College Park\n       </a>\n       which was founded as the Maryland Agricultural College in 1856 and became a public\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Land_grant_college" title="Land grant college">\n        land grant college\n       </a>\n       in 1864.\n       <a href="/wiki/Towson_University" title="Towson University">\n        Towson University\n       </a>\n       , founded in 1866, is the state\'s second largest university. Baltimore is home to the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland,_Baltimore_County" title="University of Maryland, Baltimore County">\n        University of Maryland, Baltimore County\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Institute_College_of_Art" title="Maryland Institute College of Art">\n        Maryland Institute College of Art\n       </a>\n       . The majority of public universities in the state are affiliated with the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_System_of_Maryland" title="University System of Maryland">\n        University System of Maryland\n       </a>\n       . Two state-funded institutions,\n       <a href="/wiki/Morgan_State_University" title="Morgan State University">\n        Morgan State University\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_College_of_Maryland" title="St. Mary\'s College of Maryland">\n        St. Mary\'s College of Maryland\n       </a>\n       , as well as two federally funded institutions, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Uniformed_Services_University_of_the_Health_Sciences" title="Uniformed Services University of the Health Sciences">\n        Uniformed Services University of the Health Sciences\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Academy" title="United States Naval Academy">\n        United States Naval Academy\n       </a>\n       , are not affiliated with the University System of Maryland.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_College_(Annapolis/Santa_Fe)" title="St. John\'s College (Annapolis/Santa Fe)">\n        St. John\'s College\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Annapolis,_Maryland" title="Annapolis, Maryland">\n        Annapolis, Maryland\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington_College" title="Washington College">\n        Washington College\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Chestertown,_Maryland" title="Chestertown, Maryland">\n        Chestertown, Maryland\n       </a>\n       , both private institutions, are the two oldest colleges in the state, and are among the oldest in the country. Other private institutions include\n       <a href="/wiki/Mount_St._Mary%27s_University" title="Mount St. Mary\'s University">\n        Mount St. Mary\'s University\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/McDaniel_College" title="McDaniel College">\n        McDaniel College\n       </a>\n       (formerly known as Western Maryland College),\n       <a href="/wiki/Hood_College" title="Hood College">\n        Hood College\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Stevenson_University" title="Stevenson University">\n        Stevenson University\n       </a>\n       (formerly known as Villa Julie College),\n       <a href="/wiki/Loyola_University_Maryland" title="Loyola University Maryland">\n        Loyola University Maryland\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Goucher_College" title="Goucher College">\n        Goucher College\n       </a>\n       , among others.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_libraries">\n        Public libraries\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Public libraries">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Maryland\'s 24 public library systems deliver public education for everyone in the state of Maryland through a curriculum that comprises three pillars: Self-Directed Education (books and materials in all formats, e-resources), Research Assistance &amp; Instruction (individualized research assistance, classes for students of all ages), and Instructive &amp; Enlightening Experiences (e.g., Summer Reading Clubs, author events).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Maryland\'s library systems include, in part:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_County_Public_Library" title="Baltimore County Public Library">\n         Baltimore County Public Library\n        </a>\n        System\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Cecil_County_Public_Library" title="Cecil County Public Library">\n         Cecil County Public Library\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Enoch_Pratt_Free_Library" title="Enoch Pratt Free Library">\n         Enoch Pratt Free Library\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Harford_County_Public_Library" title="Harford County Public Library">\n         Harford County Public Library\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Howard_County_Public_Library" title="Howard County Public Library">\n         Howard County Public Library\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Montgomery_County_Public_Libraries" title="Montgomery County Public Libraries">\n         Montgomery County Public Libraries\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Prince_George%27s_County_Memorial_Library_System" title="Prince George\'s County Memorial Library System">\n         Prince George\'s County Memorial Library System\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        St. Mary\'s County Public Library\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">\n         <a href="#cite_note-154">\n          [154]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Many of the library systems have established formalized partnerships with other educational institutions in their counties and regions.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">\n        Sports\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Sports">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg/220px-CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg/330px-CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg/440px-CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Oriole_Park_at_Camden_Yards" title="Oriole Park at Camden Yards">\n          Oriole Park at Camden Yards\n         </a>\n         , home of the\n         <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">\n          Baltimore Orioles\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:M%26T_Bank_Stadium_DoD.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1682" data-file-width="2500" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/M%26T_Bank_Stadium_DoD.jpg/220px-M%26T_Bank_Stadium_DoD.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/M%26T_Bank_Stadium_DoD.jpg/330px-M%26T_Bank_Stadium_DoD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/M%26T_Bank_Stadium_DoD.jpg/440px-M%26T_Bank_Stadium_DoD.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:M%26T_Bank_Stadium_DoD.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/M%26T_Bank_Stadium" title="M&amp;T Bank Stadium">\n          M&amp;T Bank Stadium\n         </a>\n         , home of the\n         <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Ravens" title="Baltimore Ravens">\n          Baltimore Ravens\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Maryland" title="Sports in Maryland">\n        Sports in Maryland\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Maryland#Athletes" title="List of people from Maryland">\n        List of people from Maryland \xc2\xa7\xc2\xa0Athletes\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       With two major metropolitan areas, Maryland has a number of major and minor professional sports franchises. Two\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">\n        National Football League\n       </a>\n       teams play in Maryland, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Ravens" title="Baltimore Ravens">\n        Baltimore Ravens\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore,_Maryland" title="Baltimore, Maryland">\n        Baltimore\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington_Redskins" title="Washington Redskins">\n        Washington Redskins\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Landover,_Maryland" title="Landover, Maryland">\n        Landover\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Baltimore_Colts" title="History of the Baltimore Colts">\n        Baltimore Colts\n       </a>\n       represented the NFL in Baltimore from 1953 to 1983 before moving to\n       <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis" title="Indianapolis">\n        Indianapolis\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">\n        Baltimore Orioles\n       </a>\n       are the state\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">\n        Major League Baseball\n       </a>\n       franchise. The\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">\n        National Hockey League\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington_Capitals" title="Washington Capitals">\n        Washington Capitals\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">\n        National Basketball Association\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington_Wizards" title="Washington Wizards">\n        Washington Wizards\n       </a>\n       formerly played in Maryland, until the construction of an arena in Downtown D.C. in 1997 (originally known as MCI Center, renamed\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Verizon_Center" title="Verizon Center">\n        Verizon Center\n       </a>\n       in 2006).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Maryland enjoys considerable historical repute for the talented sports players of its past, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Cal_Ripken_Jr." title="Cal Ripken Jr.">\n        Cal Ripken Jr.\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth" title="Babe Ruth">\n        Babe Ruth\n       </a>\n       . In 2012,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Baltimore_Sun" title="The Baltimore Sun">\n         The Baltimore Sun\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       published a list of Maryland\'s top ten athletes in the state\'s history. The list includes Babe Ruth, Cal Ripken Jr,\n       <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Unitas" title="Johnny Unitas">\n        Johnny Unitas\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Brooks_Robinson" title="Brooks Robinson">\n        Brooks Robinson\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Frank_Robinson" title="Frank Robinson">\n        Frank Robinson\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ray_Lewis" title="Ray Lewis">\n        Ray Lewis\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Phelps" title="Michael Phelps">\n        Michael Phelps\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jimmie_Foxx" title="Jimmie Foxx">\n        Jimmie Foxx\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jim_Parker_(American_football)" title="Jim Parker (American football)">\n        Jim Parker\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Wes_Unseld" title="Wes Unseld">\n        Wes Unseld\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">\n        <a href="#cite_note-155">\n         [155]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Other professional sports franchises in the state include five affiliated\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minor_league_baseball" title="Minor league baseball">\n        minor league baseball\n       </a>\n       teams, one\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independent_league_baseball" title="Independent league baseball">\n        independent league baseball\n       </a>\n       team, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_Blast_(current)" title="Baltimore Blast (current)">\n        Baltimore Blast\n       </a>\n       indoor soccer team, two indoor football teams, three low-level outdoor soccer teams, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bayhawks" title="Chesapeake Bayhawks">\n        Chesapeake Bayhawks\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Lacrosse" title="Major League Lacrosse">\n        Major League Lacrosse\n       </a>\n       . Maryland is also home to one of the three races in horse racing\'s annual Triple Crown, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Preakness_Stakes" title="Preakness Stakes">\n        Preakness Stakes\n       </a>\n       , which is run every spring at\n       <a href="/wiki/Pimlico_Race_Course" title="Pimlico Race Course">\n        Pimlico Race Course\n       </a>\n       in Baltimore.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Congressional_Country_Club" title="Congressional Country Club">\n        Congressional Country Club\n       </a>\n       has hosted three golf tournaments for the\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Open_(golf)" title="U.S. Open (golf)">\n        U.S. Open\n       </a>\n       and a\n       <a href="/wiki/PGA_Championship" title="PGA Championship">\n        PGA Championship\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The official state sport of Maryland, since 1962, is\n       <a href="/wiki/Jousting" title="Jousting">\n        jousting\n       </a>\n       ; the official team sport since 2004 is\n       <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse" title="Lacrosse">\n        lacrosse\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">\n        <a href="#cite_note-156">\n         [156]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Lacrosse_Hall_of_Fame" title="National Lacrosse Hall of Fame">\n        National Lacrosse Hall of Fame\n       </a>\n       is located on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Johns Hopkins University">\n        Johns Hopkins University\n       </a>\n       campus in Baltimore. In 2008, intending to promote physical fitness for all ages, walking became the official state exercise. Maryland is the first state with an official state exercise.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">\n        <a href="#cite_note-157">\n         [157]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span Archived from the original on August 30, 2007\n           <span class="reference-accessdate">\n            . Retrieved\n            <span class="nowrap">\n             August 30,\n            </span>\n            2007\n           </span>\n           .\n          </cite>\n          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Maryland+Animals&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.sailor.lib.md.us%2FMD_topics%2Fres%2Fenv_ani.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMaryland">\n           <span style="display:none;">\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          <span class="citation-comment" style="display:none; color:#33aa33; margin-left:0.3em">\n           CS1 maint: BOT: original-url status unknown (\n           <a href="/wiki/Category:CS1_maint:_BOT:_original-url_status_unknown" title="Category:CS1 maint: BOT: original-url status unknown">\n            link\n           </a>\n           )\n          </span>\n         </span>\n        </li>\n        <li id="cite_note-34">\n         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n          <b>\n           <a href="#cite_ref-34">\n            ^\n           </a>\n          </b>\n         </span>\n         <span class="reference-text">\n          <cite class="citation web">\n           Therres, Glenn (Fall 2007).\n           <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20110419203123/http://www.dnr.state.md.us/naturalresource/fall2007/lions.pdf" rel="nofollow">\n            "Lions in our mountains? The mystery of cougars in Maryland"\n           </a>\n           <span style="font-size:85%;">\n            (PDF)\n           </span>\n           .\n           <i>\n            Wildlife and Heritage\n           </i>\n           . Maryland Department of Natural Resources. Archived from\n           <a class="external text" href="http://www.dnr.state.md.us/naturalresource/fall2007/lions.pdf" rel="nofollow">\n            the original\n           </a>\n           <span style="font-size:85%;">\n            (PDF)\n           </span>\n           on April 19, 2011\n           <span class="reference-accessdate">\n            . Retrieved\n            <span class="nowrap">\n             July 6,\n            </span>\n            2009\n           </span>\n           .\n           <q>\n            Historically bobcats were distributed statewide but during the post colonization period densities began to plummet. By the mid-1900s, populations had probably reached all-time lows, with remnant populations existing only in western Maryland. This prompted the Department of Natural Resources (DNR) to classify them as a state-listed "Species of Special Concern." During the past quarter century, occupied range and densities have increased markedly. Results from the annual Bowhunter Survey and the Hunter Mail survey have identified bobcat sightings in 14 of Maryland\'s 23 counties. Currently, bobcats have dual legal classification in Maryland. In addition to the Species of Special Concern designation, they are also defined as a Game Animal / Furbearer with a closed harvest season.\n           </q>\n          </cite>\n          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Wildlife+and+Heritage&amp;rft.atitle=Lions+in+our+mountains%3F+The+mystery+of+cougars+in+Maryland&amp;rft.ssn=summer&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.aulast=Therres&amp;rft.aufirst=Glenn&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.dnr.state.md.us%2Fnaturalresource%2Ffall2007%2Flions.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMaryland">\n           <span style="display:none;">\n           </span>\n          </span>\n         </span>\n        </li>\n        <li id="cite_note-35">\n         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n          <b>\n           <a href="#cite_ref-35">\n            ^\n           </a>\n          </b>\n         </span>\n         <span class="reference-text">\n          <cite class="citation web">\n           <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20110815030808/http://www.dnr.state.md.us/wildlife/Hunt_Trap/furbearers/coyote.asp" rel="nofollow">\n            "Coyotes in Maryland"\n           </a>\n           . Maryland Department of Natural Resources. Archived from\n           <a class="external text" href="http://www.dnr.state.md.us/wildlife/Hunt_Trap/furbearers/coyote.asp" rel="nofollow">\n            the original\n           </a>\n           on August 15, 2011\n           <span class="reference-accessdate">\n            . Retrieved\n            <span class="nowrap">\n             September 16,\n            </span>\n            2011\n           </span>\n           .\n           <q>\n            Coyotes were historically a western species with core populations found west of the Mississippi River. Alterations and/or elimination of competing predators during the post-European colonization period facilitated rapid range expansion into eastern North America during the 20th Century. Established populations now occur in every state and province in North America. Coyotes are a relatively new addition to local ecosystems, and were first documented in Maryland during 1972. Initial substantiated sightings occurred in Cecil, Frederick and Washington counties. Since that time population densities and occupied range have expanded incrementally and coyotes now occur statewide.\n           </q>\n          </cite>\n          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Coyotes+in+Maryland&amp;rft.pub=Maryland+Department+of+Natural+Resources&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.dnr.state.md.us%2Fwildlife%2FHunt_Trap%2Ffurbearers%2Fcoyote.asp&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMaryland">\n           <span style="display:none;">\n           </span>\n          </span>\n         </span>\n        </li>\n        <li id="cite_note-horse-36">\n         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n          ^\n          <a href="#cite_ref-horse_36-0">\n           <sup>\n            <i>\n             <b>\n              a\n             </b>\n            </i>\n           </sup>\n          </a>\n          <a href="#cite_ref-horse_36-1">\n           <sup>\n            <i>\n             <b>\n              b\n             </b>\n            </i>\n           </sup>\n          </a>\n          <a href="#cite_ref-horse_36-2">\n           <sup>\n            <i>\n             <b>\n              c\n             </b>\n            </i>\n           </sup>\n          </a>\n         </span>\n         <span class="reference-text">\n          <cite class="citation web">\n           <a class="external text" href="http://www.assateagueisland.com/wildlife/pony.htm" rel="nofollow">\n            "Assateague Island National Seashore wild Ponies"\n           </a>\n           .
